From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan  5 18:28:56 1994
From: csc@pilot.njin.net (Sean Casey)
Date: Wed, 5 Jan 94 21:28:46 EST
Subject: Universal Groove, bah.
Status: 


[This review is a little late, but might be of interest.]

For the second (and last) time, Greg and I were pretty dissapointed in
Universe Groove at Thunder Bay.

Okay the positive technical details: Cool space, well ventilated, free
water, sufficient volume.

Bad technical details: No ins-n-outs (changed since last time), DJ in
main room is in separate room and invisible, speakers hanging from
ceiling with no real sound imaging.

But two things really killed this party:

One was persistent sound problems in the smaller room. Carlos was
spinning, and man he was jamming, and there'd be a great vibe for 15
minutes, then the speaker would blow out. Every time I walked into the
room, there'd be a great vibe, or everyone would be standing around
looking like they wanted there to be a great vibe. Poor Carlos, having
to deal with all that (they even swapped out mixers mid-party).

But what _really_ killed it was the crowd. I've never seen so many
people at an event for there to be no vibe at all. Lots of attitude.
Everyone standing around trying to look cool. Maybe 15-20% of the
people were dancing, and I don't know why not because the music was
good enough to dance to. It makes me wonder if it just isn't a cool
place to hang out. The place had a very negative atmosphere. Could
have used a very large jar of E.

Next time YSH is cancelled, I think we're going to try out Spacelab.
Would've this time, but I forgot my rave guide and phone numbers.

I don't recommend this event. We've been two or three times now cause
we wanted to give it a chance, and we've always had more fun listening
to mix tapes in the car on the way back. We *had* to listen to those
mix tapes to cleanse out all that negative vibe we picked up.

Sean

From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan  5 18:57:23 1994
From: csc@pilot.njin.net (Sean Casey)
Date: Wed, 5 Jan 94 21:57:09 EST
Subject: NYE party at the Resort!
Status: 

[I apologise for this late review...]

That was just a killer killer awesome party. Good vibes, good friends,
good music, good space, good visuals.

I can't resist giving a technical review first ;)

Indoor and outdoor space. Ins and outs. Two bathrooms. Excellent
sound. No security. Price: $0. Fresh DJs. No brassiere and booty
gangsta molls (but one temporarily upset goth). Free beer. Free
munchies. Great visuals. Good directions. Lots of chillout space. Pool
and hottub but they didn't look like you'd really want to use them...
Friendly promoters. Free videogames.

Yum :).

Bryce started out with "The History of Dance Music", playing, as
someone pointed out, YMCA, as well as "I'm Turning Japanese" and other
goodies. (What? No Jane's Addiction? :)) And *everyone* was getting
into it. Finally he faded out for the countdown and we all did
champagne and massive amounts of hugging.

And then, as if to say "Welcome to the 90s", he cut into some
delicious acid trance. God I loved that moment, that transition. After
listening to all that disco and stuff, _that_ was cool.

And then Ethan opened with that wailing siren Vapor Space cut, and
dove into one of the most incredible, sick, twisted acid trance sets
I've ever heard. He just fucking blew Tim and I away. Tim kept coming
over to me with permagrin, muttering "Sick...sick..."

And then Tamara got her chance (of course she did, or I was going to
make a scene) and spun some slightly less sick but awesome good
trance, perfect for winding the night down. I cooked off a lot of
calories as I am wont to do when the music's that good.

We crashed there that night, and the next day woke up to redwood
forests, birds, and warm sunshine. A day spent at the beach and in
Santa Cruz topped off a perfect weekend.

Many many thanks to Steve for putting it together and throwing a
perfect house party. And thanks to Ethan, Bryce, and Tamara for the
equipment and great music. Thanks to the SFRavers that showed for
bringing your good vibes and for being family. And a very special
thanks to the hosts for inviting us to their house so we could trash
it.

House parties! Yes!

Sean

From sfraves-owner  Thu Jan  6 11:40:20 1994
From: "Mike Romo*" <mike_romo*@quickmail.apple.com>
Date: 6 Jan 1994 11:36:24 -0800
Subject: Wired!
Status: 

                      Subject:                              Time:  11:39 AM
  OFFICE MEMO         Wired!                                Date:  1/6/94
Well, Geoff asked for a report---

I really had a ball at Wired, actually.  The space was really cool, I dug the
elevator, and I had a good time watching the Macworlders try to understand the
dancers (and vice versa).  I  came in during the second half of Farina's set, a
good farina set, housey, good.  I hadn't head Evil eddie Richards before, but I
really dug his very tribal sound.  It brings me back to last year, when San
Francisco was really into the whole tribal thing.  Totally cool.  Josh came on,
but he only played for about 20 minutes and then it was over (around 2:15).  I
had a good time doing the coat check, as I was tired of dancing, and just want
to hang out and meet people.  Huge space!  
Best part of the night was when someone knocked over this huge vase of really
incredible flowers.  A LOT of people got free flowers that night!  Fun time,
well worth the drive.  I hope one or two more parties can be put in that space
before Wired moves in!

Josh said that Come/Unity was going off when he left, so I suppose it was up to
its usual awesomeness.  

see ya!
m i k e
(anyone know of any good MacWorld parties on Friday?  I have to go with my
group from work and want to make the best of it.)

Hope everyone had a great New Year's...after the big weekend, it seems
like the promoters forgot about this Friday.  So maybe you'll want to 
check out Corduroy City.  Saturday has a couple of interesting parties;
one is at the I-Beam, great location for Haight area residents, and the
other is a Wicked presentation at the much-maligned 16th & Harrison space.
I dunno how that'll work.

Sunday morning, Sunday Soul and DNA rush in quickly to fill the void
left by the end of Boogie Buffet; Mushroom Jazz has been great on
Mondays and Together returns with a stellar lineup on Tuesday.
Wednesday, you might want to check out the Bulletproof party at Miss
Pearl's, and next Thursday, hopefully Your Sisters' House will finally
return...

Hello:   Sunday Soul, Stone Groove, the Loft, Grin
Goodbye: Boogie Buffet (back in the spring)

From sfraves-owner  Thu Jan  6 14:18:33 1994
From: trance@netcom.com (Tamara Palmer)
Date: Thu, 6 Jan 1994 14:18:46 -0800 (PST)
Subject: Re: So how was ComeUnity?
Status: 

> 
> I was knocked out with the flu last night so I missed both
> ComeUnity and the WiReD party. Anybody go to either?
> What did I miss?

I went to both and had a great time at both. After a few 
problems getting into the Wired party (they opened the
dorrs 40 minutes late so we were all standing out in the
cold), we went up to find Mark Farina spinning a really
jazzy set, which I liked, but it sounded lost echoing off
the walls of this huge loft/warehouse? space. You had to
stand close to the DJ to really hear what was going on.
They had a separate area with an ambient room,bars, and
tables, and at the beginning there seemed to be a sort
of segregation, suit-and-tie set in this room and ravers
in the other...it broke down a little later in the evening
(but eventually the corporate set got tired and went home).
Eddie Richards took over after Mark (does he still use the
"Evil" nickname?) and played some upbeat stuff (like stuff
on Murk). Josh came on after that, but I didn't stay in that
room during his set...I noticed that he tapes his record
labels and I really hate that (I think it smacks of
elitism but that's another post altogether).

After Wired closed down at 2, we headed over to ComeUnity.
It was packed and Jeno was playing in the main room...I
enjoyed his stuff since I haven't heard him since he came
down to LA about a month ago and played a lot of stuff that
I just didn't like. The lights were gettting too annoying so I
crashed out in the ambient room (NOISY ambient room!) and 
listened to Dubtribe lay down some cool live ambient...nice way
to wind down the evening.

Highlight of the evening: free money from Mike!!

	There's a Verbum magazine "Digital Be-In" on Friday night at the
	Fashion Center-Grand Atrium Theatre, 699 Eighth Street, in 
	San Francisco.  Here's the blurb:

	"Experience the multimedia concert Featuring live music - with
	 stunning visuals that YOU help create - Global Vortex (w/ members
	 of the Grateful Dead), Scott Page ( of Pink Floyd) and the Hang 
	 Dynasty, Amy X Neuberg, Trance Mission, Marimba Pacifica and 
	 more!  Plus: the West Coast debut of the SimGraphics Virtual
	 Mark Twain - as co-host of the event.

	 HEAR the views of cultural visionaries and artists including
	 Timothy Leary, Ted Nelson, John Barlow and Thomas Dolby.

	 EXPLORE Virtual Reality Interactive works by Peter Gabriel, 

	 David Bowie, Howie Mandel.  Amazing new products from AT&T, 
	 Apple Computer, Fractal Design and others.

	 ENJOY great food and drink from the chefs of Portico and Miss 
	 Pearl's"

	 This thing is somewhat pricey ($25) but is quite a scene.  I went

From sfraves-owner  Fri Jan  7 08:56:50 1994
From: nrg@netcom.com (Ethan I. Miller)
Date: Fri, 7 Jan 1994 08:58:44 -0800
Subject: SpaceLab Review
Status: 

Holy shit! SpaceLab was totally, completely out of this world last night.
Best music I've ever heard in San Francisco -- no joke.

Kevin got things going, was followed by chris who provided serious subsonic
bass therapy as an intro to Jonas spinning the sickest, hardest non-stop
high-energy acid trance I've ever heard. Which was only the beginning; he
was joined live by miguel playing what they described as the "acid boxes" a
bunch of roland boxes 303, 909, and I think I heard him say a 707? I
watched Jonah pull of a mind-bending 5-minute vinyl mix while miguel just
shredded with tweaky acid warps, phases etc. Ultimately they let the vinyl
stop and just jammed on the boxes simultaneously. Live acid is amazing!

They were followed by Alex who continued in like form, totally rearranging
my mind. He appears to a master of the line switch, using it to apply
gate-like to effects to vocals, synths etc. Smoked the vinyl...

Check this one out next time, you may never be the same afterward. 
Grin  :)

still reeling
ethan

From sfraves-owner  Fri Jan  7 18:07:40 1994
From: JMRTNKO DSGN ETC SFCA <martinko@netcom.com>
Date: Fri, 7 Jan 1994 17:42:33 -0800 (PST)
Subject: Re: B-Day Spacelab
Status: 


Yikes! What more can be said? I know where I'll be on Thursday nights. 

I was feeling lazy, so I took the Mission bus instead of walking (only 9 
blocks) and got in around 12:30. Luckily I hadn't missed much (except all 
the great music). Having Miguel's party there was the icing on the cake. 
Everybody coming for it got in for half-price and the place was full of 
his friends. It was like a San Anselmo field trip (now make sure you get 
this note signed by your parents, wear your name tag, &c...). What really 
amused me was the number of Macworldites. If you didn't think the blinky 
red pendant wouldn't give you away...Oh well, as usual, the music was 
amazing. I was waiting around for Miguel to play and around 2 finally he 
and Jonas broke into an acidy-jackhammer set. The dance area was packed 
(for SpaceLab). My ears are still ringing. Unfortunately, it went on only 
for about 15 minutes. We wanted more, but after all, it's their show. 

This is probably too vague, but there's a track Jonas plays every week 
that I *must* know the name of. It came on before the set with Miguel. 
Simple track really, just a beat and simple melody from what sounds like 
an old Hammond organ with a descending piano bit over it. At SpaceLab, 
whever this thing comes on, it's like a physical command to get to the 
dancefloor. I guess I'll have to make it a point to ask next week.

When I left around 3:30, there were still quite a few folks left, and the 
music didn't give any hint of stopping. I hated to leave, but work-week 
fatigue was setting in. So nice to be able to walk home instead of drive. 
Hope to see you there next Thurs. JMAR, as usual.

From sfraves-owner  Fri Jan  7 19:18:20 1994
From: jsl@netcom.com (John S. Lee)
Date: Fri, 7 Jan 1994 19:18:43 -0800
Subject: 94 - Start your engines...
Status: 

Just got off the phone with a well known personality here on the net, then
got on the phone with James, and re-etab contacts with hosts of others.  Of
course, all on Company time.

One person I will definitely book is Sassy Lime - Disco Detective.
She spun right before, I think, Dani at the last boggie buffet.  She popped
out of nowhere and is a really good.  Mixes that 70's funk & soul so
fucking well I made a point of getting her # right off.  She's booked.

Loren (I need to hear him spin soon) & John Howard are the other two I have
in mind for a few things in 94.  Brad as well is another contender who's
shit should be ballistic here in SF by now, but lack of exposure has kept
him back...I'll do my part.

Which brings up another recurring question on the list.  Female DJ's.  I am
not going to go on and on about this, but something that happened recently,
made this stick out in my mind:

Seth H., after listening to me go on about contacts, and tapes, got my
address and sent me a tape.  It got here in a few days, and barely a week
after he promised me one.  The tape has (as of today), been forwarded to
two of my friends who like some of the harder edge stuff, and are in
positions to hire DJ's.  Seth H. took the time, did the do, and now his
tape is being circulated.

I hope that the female DJ's, who want bookings, do one thing SORELY lacking
from them over the past couple of years (sans Niki, Dani, & Jan), start
promoting themselves.  I would love to hear some new talent come from some
new ladies this year, but I won't be going to the four corners to find
them. I hope I don't have to hear the "stuff" about female DJ's not getting
booked.  Becuase the FIRST thing I will ask them is "Do you have a tape?",
then "Where will you be spinning next?"



Calling all...

I am looking for some stuff for '94.  First, if you know anyone who can
toast, rap, or do spoken word let me know.  I am looking for a more soulful
flavor (like Digable Planets, et al), and good voice.  Improv a plus, but
if you have some records that you've practiced with, and have a set, I'm
looking for you.

Next, I am looking for African American females who can do the do on the
decks.  If they are versed in hip-hop, deep house, & dub. Let me know how I
can get ahold of them.

Next, I am looking for female talent in general.  Someone who can do the do
with acid jazz, house, & deep house.  If you know of anyone lemme know.

Thats' my shopping list for '94.  Just leave me their # and I'll call them up.

C'ya,
John

From sfraves-owner  Fri Jan  7 19:27:10 1994

Subject: Re: SpaceLab Review

Right on, Ethan!
SpaceLab is definitely my favorite club in SF.  The place
was PACKED, partly because of Miguel Cell Orchestra's b-day.  Maybe they'll
start using the downstairs?!!  As always, the music was mindblowing, but I
have to say,I think Alex might just get a teensy weensy bit trigger happy with
the line/transform switch.  When it works, it REALLY works, pumping up the
crowd and causing scattered shouts of approval, but if the timing is only
slightly off, it sounds bad and makes it difficult to keep the dancin'
groove.  This is my only little (note: LITTLE) gripe about the dj'ing. 
Jonah ripped it up bigtime, as did Miguel and his handy dandy 303.  The
only other complaint I have is that it's on the same day as YSH :(

Cap'n Crunch - Umm, just thought I should put you in here somewhere
All the Bootstores in SF and Berkeley - For having a hoakey collection of 
  boots, I finally found a pair of steeltoed Cat's in LA
Spaghetti Western - Hey, the food is okay, but I think they are 
  overcharging for the ambiance (come back Delta's Depression Dough)
Housewares - For finally letting me see a pair of Ambiance Pants (?) and 
  having an NE Raves sticker up (Susie?).

And to all the folks I met and saw again, it was a blast.  I dig your 
scene, quite different than the east (observations withheld, do I look like 
flame bait?).  But it is nice to get back to familiar friends, the net, 
work, writing and a stable household.

Dan

Ps. Bryce, I was very impressed with that first set on New Years.  Who 
would have thought they would dance to that stuff, I almost died 
laughing, but you pulled it off.  That's style.

and hopefully much trippiness as well :)   I don't think hip-hop
will be fusing much with hard-acid-techno, although "techno-hop"
could be quite interesting...

From sfraves-owner  Mon Jan 10 03:58:59 1994
From: crunch@netcom.com (John Draper)
Date: Mon, 10 Jan 1994 03:59:30 -0800
Subject: Weeks raves as I see them...
Status: 


(This is rather long)

This weeks rave scene as I saw it
=================================

		By
	  John T. Draper
	  "Cap'n Crunch"
	  
   This week,  I had Mac World Expo to deal with,  so this sorta
mucked up my usual raving this week,  but I did get in some raving
in some strange sort of way.    I guess I'll start off by my 
observations of the Wired Magazine's First aniversary party.

   The Wired party was FREE.   Probably the best part about it,
but for me,   it was a togetherness between the MacWorld folks
who I have known for many years,   as all of my "Out of towners"
were there,  and for the very first time,   they came together
with all of my friends and family of the SF Ravers.    It was a
strange mix in a way.   All these "suits" together with all the 
ravers.   Quite a few Mac Worlders were on the dance floor,  even
a few suits.   It was the first time any of my Mac Worlders has 
ever seen me dancing.,  It got quite a few "double takes".

   I would guess there were about 500 folks (Possibly more),  because
I got in rather late,  after checking into a few other MacWorld parties,
and finding them to be total duds.    Yukk!!  After all that time,
hustling for invites,  those parties requiring invites seem to be
really bad.    Good free food and drinks,   but for some reason,
I find schmoosing with ravers much more enjoyable.    At any rate,
when I arrived at the Wired party,   one of the DJ's was playing some
rather slow jazzy stuff.    Good dancable music,   but I decided to
schmoose with my "out of towner" friends and prep my head for
the evening.   After I noticed the music picking up,  I headed
over to the dance floor,  and found all my SFRaver friends getting
into some pretty good energetic stuff,  all huddled by the speakers.
For some reason,  the sound level didn't have as much of a "punchey"
punping sound that I like.    The Mac Worlders were way out away from
the speakers,  but there WAS some good mixture out there.    Lots
of room,  and not that crowded.    The DJ's were really good,   playing
some good newer stuff along with the usual "housey" sound.

   After the Wired party,  I headed over to Come/Unity at 1015
Folsom and WOW!!   AWSOME!!   It was almost WICKED in nature,
and super crowded.    I think it was because I told a lot of
Mac Worlders about Come/Unity, as it wasn't on any of the Mac
World Party lists.    As the very first thing I did,  was to
go to the BMUG (Berkeley Mac Users Group),  and get the latest
MacWorld party list.   WHAT!!  Come/unity not on the list??  
C'm on folks,   you can do metter that THAT!!   It was hard
for me to explain that Come/Unity wasn't a party you would
want to miss.   And they would say,  "Why isn't it on the list?"
I would say,  "It's a SPECAIL party, you won't want to miss it".
It certainly lived up to its expectations.    It was pumpin hard
and strong,  putting 1015's sound system to it's limit.   I would'nt
want to guess how many people were there,   but it was a LOT.
It lasted until 7:30 am,  which was also super great!!!   An
ALL NIGHTER!!  in the middle of the week.   After that was
over,  I headed home for a shower,  change back into my suit,
and headed back to MacWorld to see the General Magic demo.

   After MacWorld,  I was able to sneak into the Todd Rundgren's
private party at the Exploratorium.   I know Todd Personally,  cause
I helped him with a Mac Programming problem a few years ago.    

  The food was excellent,  and free drinks,   so I hosed down a lot
of it,  cause I was starving.   Nothing was really going to get
started musically until later,  but we all had fun,  playing with all 
the science "hands on" exhibits that make the Exploratorium so 
famious.   I sure met a lot of old friends I haven't seen for ions,
and learned that you can put a straight bar through a curved slot,
played with ions,   and generated high voltage sparks.  Whoopee!! :-)

   Todd's "Stage" had a huge mixture of roland electronic drums,
a few synthesyzers,   and a huge array of TV Monitors sitting above
the round stage in the middle of the main exhibit floor.   The
round stage had a sort of metallic floor around it,   then in the 
inside,   the midi equipment,  and on top of that,  the monitors.

   Todd explained the "Protocol" to his "Interactive performance"
where the audience was to have a part of it.    They had rubber
sharks,  dinosaurs,  and other things hanging from rods connected
to the top of the round stage.   Todd explaned that when the green
light goes on,   the audience was invited to dance on the round stage.
When Yellow, the GoGo Dancers had that area.   When "red",  it means
that only Todd could be up there.   When I heard that there was this
possibility of dancing up there,   I started heading towards the
front.   I wanted to be in on this gig.   All the geeks from Mac
World sorta hung back taking it all in.

   Todd went crazy,  playing some new stuff I haven't hear on his
new Video,   then went into some of his popular stuff.   All during the
show,   the green light would go on,  and everyone would jump up on
the stage and start dancing.    People would sorta march around the
stage.    As I looked out in the audience,  all my Mac Geek friends
were totally surprised to see me up there acting like a nut,  having
a total ball.   Todd would jump off the stage,  shaking the hands
of the dancers,  then handing out drum stick to people,   showing
them where their drums are,  and it was a total interactive jam
session to end all jam sessions.   The interactive audience went crazy,
while SOME geeks and the suits were schmoozing,  totally unaware
of the insane amount of jamming going on.

   After Todds show,  I schmoozed around for a while,  talking to
old friends,  and telling them where the Space lab party is located.
Naturally,  it wasn't on any of the Mac World party lists,  and
the Mac Worlders were just starving and drooling over the prospect
of learning of a new PARTY.   I told them,  you don't want to miss
this one,  and it goes till 4 am.    Wish I had those Space lab flyers,
it would have made my life easier.    So I made sure they all knew
how to get there,  as I told about a 150 of my friends about it.
It was at the Trocidero.

   Sure enough.... as I arrived,  so did a LOT of my Mac World
friends,  and they would say WOW!!  Great party.   And it sure
lived up to it.    Absolutely AWSOME Acid Techno stuff,  and
after not sleeping the night before,  it was just what I needed.
Good fast music.   Great German stuff.  Ohhh!!  I wish someday
to get back to Germany and attend one of their raves.   I went
totally insane on the dance floor.   Met a raver friend from Seattle
I met while attending the BASIC rave up there a month ago.    He
was also at the previous evenings Come/Unity party.   Anyway,  the
music was the best I've heard since Darcy spun at the last "Your
Sisters House" party.   All my Mac World freinds really dug it.
One would come up to me and say "How to you hear about these parties".
I said "It was on the raves list",  then explain the SFRaves calander
to them.    It was all over much to soon for me,   Yukk!!  4 am,  and
nothing going on...   Guess I'll go home and try to sleep.   I managed
to trance out for a few hours at least before I had to get over to
Mac World again in the morning.

   Friday morning....  Time to hustle around at Mac World,   and
prepare for yet another evening of partying.    I knew that I would
have to hustle to try and get into the DIGITAL BE-IN.  It costs
a whopping $25.... YUKKK!!   I ran into Ted Nelson on the way
to Mac World,  and he told me that Tim Leary was sick and couldn't
make this one.   Oh WOW!!  no Tim Leary this year....

   Before going to Digital Be-In,  I headed over to BMUG party
at the "Bottom of the hill" club.   I just popped in there to say
hi to the crowd,   then headed over to the Be-In.   I wanted to get
there before it started,  cause it would be easier to sneak in.
No such luck.    It already started,  but.....  Egad!!  Allan Lundell
had remembered to put me on his STAFF list.    They handed me a
STAFF sticker,  and it was FAT CITY.   Yow!! I was in...  plus
could go back stage...  omygod!!  what luck.

   I get there just as it was starting.    First I'll explain the
venue...   It's the FASHION CENTER,  a big swankey place, with
multiple stories,  and a large center.   Many rooms, stores,
and definately a multiple entertainment gig.   There were VR stations,
and the "Body Synth" people,  computer demos,  smart drinks,  and
a lot of stuff even I can't explain.    NO house music yet...  Ughh!
So I schmoose,  and take in the entertainment,  and an opportunity to
get off my feet from walking around Mac Expo all day long.  YES!!
even *I* have certain limits,  I just know what they are...

   Eventually I hear the music,  and start heading down to where
a few SFRavers are dancing.   WOW!!  good music,   volume a tad too
low,   but alright next to the speaker.   I was kickin as usual to
some pretty common stuff.    The rest of the geeks and suits were 
just sitting down,  shaking their heads as I was going crazy with
the music.   Sets were rather short,  about 20 minutes long,  and
used as filler between gigs.    The main sheebang started,  and
the acters took over the dance area.    Really good stuff,  people
on stilts grabbing other dancers and swinging them around.   Really
good high energy stuff.  Sheesh!! Wich I could dance to the stuff,
but I thought at that time,  it would be in-appropriate.   As the
gig started to really take off,  when the actors left,  everyone
made a bee-line for the dance area,   and we were off.   YOW!!
SUPER HIGH energy.  A Whole lot better than a rave.   More
band members picking up anything they can find,   bongos,  drums,
and other instruments,  and all joined in.    The dancing was awsome,
and very crowded.   Even the geeks were up there.  This was one of
the most intense primal get-togethers I've seen in a long time.

   After the main event,  things started to peter out,  as most of
the VR machines were shutting down.    But they kept the house music
going till 3 am.   I was wondering aound for a while,  trying to
decide if I want to go to Corduroy City or a private party at a 
recording studio.    I chose the recording studio.   Hung out there
with some dudes from Santa Cruz,  then headed over to Corduroy City,
but it was over by the time I got there.    I headed home for a much
needed shower,  then went to the LAST DAY of Mac World.    While
there,  I learned of yet another party.   It was the Digital Queers
gathering.

   I learned it was $25 to get in,   but I was lucky to some across
a friend who payed my way in.    It was very strange,  mostly gay
computer professionals,  video artists,  and a comedy gig.    But the
ONE thing that really made it great,  was a super surprise comedian
Robin Williams made an appearance.   The crowd stood up and just
went wild.   Robin fucused on gay related jokes,  and the place
roared with laughter.   I met Robin at a Computer Faire party
about 5 years ago,  and after the dance music started,  Robin
comes over and grabs my arm and said Hi.  WOW!  I had thought
he already left.    The music was the familiar house music on a super
wimpy sound system that distorted on the bass sounds.   Not only
that,   but the DJ apparently hasn't heard about "beat matching",
so my dancing was rather scattered,  besides that,  my banged up
knee was giving me problems,  not helped by all that walking around
at Mac World.    By that tim,  I only had 2 hours sleep in 4 days,
and was ready to do a full system shut down.    Anyway,  it was
a really great 4 days of trade shows and parties.  I got lots of
yoga to catch up on,   so don't plan on going out for at least
3 days.

Later...
CC

> "It is the boldest tactic in a campaign that began with improving lighting,

This is about the stupidest tactic for combating drug dealing that
I can think of.  I think it has more to do with phone vandalism
then "drug dealing" (besides, I'm sure they are not removing the phones
from which the SIGNIFICANT drug deals are made as in "O.K. I'll send my
boys to unload the tanker tonight").  I can't buy the drug dealing story,
any drug dealer who has his/her shit together should have a cellular phone
by now anyways, they don't cost that much and even the $1000 deposit
(for air time, I'm assuming the dealer doesn't have a credit card) is a
relatively small operating cost considering the potential revenue.

From sfraves-owner  Mon Jan 10 11:09:15 1994
From: alves@bethe.ucdavis.edu (David Alves)
Date: Mon, 10 Jan 94 10:53:19 PST
Subject: more jazz thoughts
Status: 




It seems like there has been a good deal of hype behind jazz/hiphop/house
music over the past year and it would be surprising if this style doesn't
get more popular and translate into parties.

I think it'll be a nice change.

Recently I heard the US3 jazz/hiphop cd and thought it was kinda dull.  It
was a rehash of other acid jazz songs with ok rapping added on.  The
super-happy piano and horn licks over flat sounding synth bass lines got
old.  The drum samples were sometimes cool. Hopefully this is not where
things are heading.

Tribe Called Quest's - Midnight Marauders is good.  I liked it.

I want to hear freakier (for lack of a better word) jazz samples and/or
original stuff.  Anthony Braxton, Ornette Coleman, Archie Shepp would
be great for really trippy music. 

My best christmas present cd was Miles Davis - Standing on the Corner
This is early seventies fusion with a bad ass Shaft kinda feel.  It is
a really cool cd.

Dave

supposed to be 'Gravitational Arch of Io' (as in moon of Jupiter). Bet 
he'll neaten up his printing on that songlist next time. Can you say 'doh!'

From sfraves-owner  Tue Jan 11 12:55:40 1994
From: lxfogel@srv.PacBell.COM (Lee Fogel)
Date: Tue, 11 Jan 94 12:55:30 PST
Subject: weekinreview
Status: 

I don't have much to add about the Wired party.  Fresh space,
fun cross-cultural pollination, loads of friends.  I had a fun.  I
might even go out and buy an issue.

ComeUnity wasn't quite the religious experience of the first and only 
other one I've been to since it's resurrection, but it was still a
great party.  The price has increased to $7, and they used the
front room for the chillout area, where Dubtribe played some truly
excellent live ambient house.  Markie/Jeno/Simon gave solid sets,
although watching Simon rifle through his records in silence for ten
minutes as he frantically searched for an appropriate encore song helped
end the party with a touch of stupidity.  I mean, the guy picks out song
after song during a 2 hour set, and then can't come up with a final one -
as though he didn't know he was going to do an encore.  I guess you just 
can't plan for those moments of pure inspiration. !-|

Did anyone go to Pucca High?  I'm real curious as to how they set up
the IBeam, and what the sound system was like.

Sunday we checked out the grand opening of Sunday Soul at the Oasis.
It was somewhat dead.  We went over to the DNA, danced a bit to some 
of Tony and Simon,  but the sound was barely adequate: the main
stacks weren't on, and neither were those Servo woofers.  There weren't 
many people there anyway, so we checked back on SS, which at 1pm was in 
need of a decent burial.  Oh, well.  We went home where I was reduced 
to watching the the N.Y. Giants warm up for the thrashing the're gonna 
give the 49'rs this Saturday.  Hope to see everyone at the Blue Cube!

- leg of eel

From sfraves-owner  Tue Jan 11 14:02:00 1994
From: JACOB%SLACVM.BITNET@Forsythe.Stanford.EDU
Date: Tue, 11 Jan 1994   13:55 -0800 (PST)
Subject: Re: weekinreview
Status: 

In-Reply-To: lxfogel@srv.pacbell.com -- 01/11/94 13:03

well, someone asked about pucca high. i went there and saw susie, giamma,
jackie, some other folx. i was not that impressed, or i should say, it did
not do that mauch for me. they walled the main room so now u have to go by
the bar to get to the dance area. the sound quality was ok, a bit distorted
at times. the musick was ok but it got too disco-y for my tastes. there
is the side room, just as u enter, on the right. that was made into the
chill room and there was some really cool mello acid jazz kinda stuff. but
the musick selection was pretty inconsistent. towards the end of my stay there
i was desperately trying to find a vibe in either rom, going back an forth
between them. left about 4 am. i would say, i'd give it a bit more  chance
to develop, but was not charmed by it yet.
take care/shalom/yeow
ovid

basically want to confirm what ovid said - a space in search of a

i did like the space, however, and would go if they got DJs i liked.

Thanks for the props Chris!

THat's no 303 -- don't need no steenkin' Roland pap-crap, not me.
That's a Yamaha SY-77 voice I "programmed" -- consists of a digital
filter sweep and an FM parameter sweep controlled by a
breath-controller. Happened upon it quite by accient... With the
appropriate breath-controller gestures, can sound more acidic than a
full bottle of "visine"....

One of these days, I hope to have time for music again...

Birmingham, UK.

SF, or Palo Alto). Or anybody know how I can mail order this?

From: Elaine.Leffler@Eng (always wash your halo with mild soap and warm water)
(yes, i'm begging for your hard-earned $$) 

During the first week of May 1994, over 500 (closer to 600
at this time) volunteers will be riding bicycles on a 500
mile route from San Francisco to Los Angeles to raise money
for the Los Angeles Gay and Lesbian Community Services Center.
My sister will be among them, and is seeking sponsors at
this time.  The requested pledge is a $100 minimum but *ANY
AMOUNT* will be greatly appreciated (a thought:  pool your 
$$ for a group donation and fight over the t-shirt).  When was
the last time YOU got to wear a hundred-dollar t-shirt?  
There are several options for payment - Visa, Mastercard, American
Express, installment plans (debits from your checking account on
a monthly basis), etc.  

The Los Angeles Gay and Lesbian Community Center is the largest
and oldest gay and lesbian social services center in the world, the
largest provider of early AIDS care in Los Angeles County with 
3,000 medically indigent clients.  The medical services offered include
psychiatry, hematology, radiology, urology, dermatology, gynecology,
neurology, and cardiology as well as an AIDS pharmacy.  The center has
a Women's HIV Clinic where over 150 women with HIV get a continuum
of special care.  It is the largest HIV test site in the nation - 
14,000 are tested each year, half of all those tested are heterosexual.
80% of all who have tested positive for HIV in L.A. County have tested
at the Center. The Center provides AIDS prevention education/inter-
vention to over 25,000 individuals per year, has 184 full-time staff
and serves over 65,000 people each year.  Programs include legal,
addiction recovery, counselling, job training, 24-bed youth shelter,
AIDS education and a computerized AIDS Information Network with 
40,000 articles on AIDS/HIV.  For more information, please contact
California AIDS Ride '94 at 213 874-7474.

The people participating in the California AIDS Ride are making a
huge commitment, not just during the weeks of the ride but also in
the months to come, training for this event.  Please consider 
sponsoring one of the riders.  Contact me via email if you are 
interested in sponsoring my sister or obtaining additional information.  
Don't forget, many companies have a gift matching program (double
your donation!) and the Center is a 501(c)3 not-for-profit organization
which makes it eligible for most of these programs.  Please spread 
the word to anyone you think might be willing to donate some bucks
to the AIDS Ride '94.

Regards,

Elaine Leffler
elef@smarmy.eng.Sun.Com


From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan 12 11:41:26 1994
From: jamiel@sybase.com (Healthier, More Manageable Hair)
Date: Wed, 12 Jan 1994 11:44:34 -0800
Subject: How to Contact Phiber Optik
Status: 

Someone mentioned looking for this info...


>Date: Tue, 11 Jan 1993 14:21:18 EST
>From: CuD Moderators <cudigest@mindvox.phantom.com>
>Subject: File 3--How to Contact Phiber Optik
>
>Emmanuel Goldstein's sensitive description of Phiber Optik's last day
>of freedom underscores the need to rethink contemporary prison
>philosophy: The punitive ethos emphasizing the "lock-'em-up" agenda
>has failed.  One of its nasty consequences includes incarcerating
>those for whom prison time serves little purpose, costs the taxpayers
>unnecessary money, and has no significant impact on crime rates.
>
>Phiber will likely spend less than 10 months in prison, much less if
>placed in an alternative program such as community corrections.
>However, prison time--especially short time--is unpleasant.  The daily
>monotony, boredom, restrictions on freedom, and deprivation of even
>the most common things that most of us take for granted, erode one's
>psyche.
>
>Schuylkill (pronounced "school-kill") FCI is in Minersville, PA in a
>mountainous, rural-agricultural area.  The central prison is fairly
>large, about 1,000. There is also a Level One (minimum security)
>satellite camp of about 290 residents where Mark will do his time.
>
>According to a prison spokesperson, Mark will live in a two-person
>cubicle. The prisoners in the camp were categorized as "non-violent,
>first-term offenders," and instances of violence, assaults, and
>attacks were described as "extremely rare." The spokesperson said that
>all camp prisoners were assigned a prison job.
>
>Those wishing to correspond with Mark or to send him packages should
>note the following:
>
>1) He may, in general, receive PAPERBACK BOOKS, soft-cover magazines,
>newspapers, and conventional letters.
>
>2) HARDCOVER BOOKS must be sent DIRECTLY from the publisher.
>
>3) He MAY NOT receive in the mail clothes, food, money, stamps, or
>anything else. No exceptions.
>
>4) There are no explicit restrictions on the types of books or
>periodicals he may receive. These are done on a case-by-case basis.
>With the exception of legal correspondence, all incoming mail is
>subject to screening by prison staff.
>
>The prison spokesperson indicated that there is no set limit on the
>number of books that Mark may receive, but emphasized that people
>should use common sense. A prisoner's personal area, he said, is
>rather small.  Sending more than one or two books at a time could
>quickly become a storage problem.
>
>Emmanuel Goldstein of 2600 Magazine will be coordinating Mark's needs.
>Those who wish to send books should contact Emmanuel at
>emmanuel@well.sf.ca.us and see what kinds of books or papers should be
>sent.
>
>Mark's address:
>
>Mark Abene  (32109-054)
>Schuylkill FCI
>Minersville, PA 17954

jamie

From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan 12 11:53:46 1994
From: pkennedy@xsoft.xerox.com (Paul F. Kennedy)
Date: 	Wed, 12 Jan 1994 11:53:22 PST
Subject: New Moon party report
Status: 


I was at the New Moon party last night. I didn't get home from work until 
9:30pm, and it wasn't until then that I picked up the msg on my answering 
machine letting me know that the New Moon was happening.  By the time I'd
finished eating and cleaning up, it was 11:00pm, then I spent some time 
on the phone and finally hit the road at midnight. 

It was held on Dusty's houseboat in Marin, apparently it was originally 
intended that it be held outdoors but Mona told me that the generator 
proved unobtaianble at the last minute, so Dusty kindly provided a backup 
site on his boat.

It took me 45 minutes to get there from San Mateo, I hadn't been to this area
of Marin before, although I guess others among you are probably familiar
with Dusty's place, I seem to remember mention of his boat in the past.

I got there about 1:00pm (the directions were a little unclear to me) and 
there were 12 others there. Sorry, don't know who was on the turntables, 
I'm bad with names, although I was introduced to one or two of the DJ's,
who seemed to rotate every 3 or 4 tracks.

I spent some time talking to Mona and she told me they'd had a discussion
before the music had started up, talking about what they wanted to accomplish
with the New Moons, fellowship, companionship etc. Everybody physically
touched everyone else, too. She wants to hold more outdoor events in the
future and is particularly keen on dancing around a fire... In my conversarion
with her there was much talk of astrology, planetary alignment, revelatory 
dreams and other worlds.  I had to be at work today so I intended to leave 
at 2:00am, as it turned out that's when it wound down anyway, Dusty wanted 
to go bye-bye's, I s'pose, and it was too cold to hang around on a beach, 
which was the original intention for the post-houseboat timeframe.

The music was low-volume and I didn't get much of an opportunity to listen to
it, I spent a lot of time locked in conversation with Dusty's housemate on
his work in the computer biz.  That and hearing all about the closest planetary
alignment in Capricorn for 300 years.  What music I did hear was acid-y, lots
of 303 noise. I think there may have been some folks learning their craft
on the turntables as well (and why not) since some of the track/beat shifts 
were less perfectly aligned than the planets.

John, I would've been able to pick you up, (if you are somewhere on the 
peninsula, that is) but I didn't read your mail until this morning. Sorry.

Pk.

From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan 12 12:09:32 1994

Date: 	Wed, 12 Jan 1994 12:09:14 PST
Subject: Billboard dance music seminar in SF next week
Status: 


There is going to be a Billboard Dance Music seminar held in San Francisco
next week, from Wednesday 19th through Friday 21st.  It is being held at 
the Pan Pacific hotel.  I understand there are going to be DJ showcases and
various panels meeting during the day discussing various aspects of
dance music. 

A friend who is travelling from LA to attend tells me that Moby will be 
among those in attendance, and will be sitting on one of the panels. 

Does anyone have any info on which DJ's will be playing ? Or on any events
taking place in the evenings loosely connected with the seminar ?

My friend Sue spoke to the event co-ordinator (I have this co-ordinators 
name and tel. number at home somewhere) and asked her why SF was the
location.  Apparently SF is seen as where it's at right now, for dance music,
although Miami was also under serious consideration at one point.

This is the first such event to be organised by Billboard and it seems to be
proving quite a challenge to piece together. I'll have a look for the contact
number at home, if anyone wants to find out more.


Pk.

From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan 12 12:44:19 1994
From: geoffw@internex.net (Geoff White)
Date: Wed, 12 Jan 1994 12:26:14 +0800
Subject: How to Contact Phiber Optik
Status: 


----- Begin Included Message -----

for the record, here's more "rules" on what to send him

-------------------from ECHO in NYC (where Mark worked) 

Mark Abene
FPC/Schuylkill
P.O. Box 670
Minersville, PA 17954


He can receive no more than five paperbacks/six magazines at once.
I didn't ask at the time if that was five books AND six mags or
five books OR six mags, I'm sorry.  To be safe I would send two
packages until we know.

Hardcover books can only be mailed directly from a publisher or
bookstore.

You can send photographs but no more than 30 and no polaroids.
That's it besides letters.  You can send nothing else.  You can send
money orders instead of care packages and he can buy some things for
himself.

As for visitors, he can have no more than four at a time.  If other
people come down to visit they must leave the prison and wait their
turn elsewhere.  Anyone that wants to visit must be approved.  Mail
Mark that you want to visit, he'll get a form from his counselor that
he will send you -- you fill it out, send it back and the approval
process begins I guess.

The person I spoke to thought Mark could have no more than 20 approved
visitors but she wasn't sure, she said Mark could find out for sure from
his counselor.




----- End Included Message -----

From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan 12 13:19:20 1994
From: "Chris Gilmore 5-8800"  <Chris.Gilmore@Forsythe.Stanford.EDU>
Date:     Wed, 12 Jan 94 13:19:03 PST
Subject:  New Moon Party Report.
Status: 

I went to the New Moon party last night.  Here are my impressions:

The night started off rather slowly.  We called the information line
around 7 pm and found that they were having difficulty finding a
generator for their outdoor space.  In any event, we were told to
call back a bit later, sooner if we knew someone with a generator.

So, we relaxed and wondered if the event was going to go off over a
bite to eat.  We called again at 8 pm and learned that they found an
indoor space for the party, so didn't need a generator after all.
This was happy news for us, so Jen, Steve, and I piled in the car
and set out on the trek from San Jose.  The indoor space was a three
story houseboat in Marin.  What an incredible space!  They had a
nice fire going in the fireplace and a view out over the water.

We were among the first to show up (10:30ish).  The DJ's hadn't
arrived yet, but the hosts had some decent trippy music on the
stereo.  We chilled in front of the fire and became familiar with
out hosts:  Dusty, Mona, and Allison.  The topic of conversation was
mostly centered around what they wanted to accomplish by holding New
Moon Raves.  This included a good deal of astrology (I understand
that Dusty is an astrologer by profession) - a topic that I've not
been exposed to very much which made it quite interesting.

After a while, the first DJ and his friends showed up.  His name is
Brad - I've never heard him before, but he's really nice and played
a good set.  (I'm quite musically ignorant, so I can't comment on
the different types of music styles that were played.  I generally
tend to put music into two categories - The stuff I like, and the
stuff I don't.  My deepest apologies to those who would have liked
more info on this aspect.  Jen is much more musically inclined, so
I'll try to get her to review the music...) He set up his equipment
and got started.  At that point, there were maybe 10 people there -
all really friendly.

There wasn't a whole lot of dancing energy in the group, but the
time was well spent in meeting and getting to know new people.  Over
the next hour or so, Brad kept spinning while we talked, danced a
bit, and ate LOTS of candy while people slowly trickled in.

Eventually, another DJ showed up and took Brad's place.  I've not
followed the DJ scene that much, so I wouldn't be able to recognize
anyone, but I do know names and such from fliers, etc.  Therefore,
you can imagine my surprise when Brad told us that the new DJ was
Robbie Hardkiss.  Robbie recognized that the people at the party
were in a pretty mellow mood, so he played some really good ambient
stuff that fit the mood of the party perfectly.  I didn't pay too
much attention to the DJ's after that, so I'm not sure who was on
after Robbie.

At about 1:30, the three of us decided that we should be heading
back to San Jose.  All three of us had to be at work by 8 this
morning and the hour and a half drive back to SJ would give us
enough time to catch a decent nap before getting ready for work.
So, we thanked our hosts and headed home.

So, here's my overall impression of this New Moon Rave:

1.  I'll definitely be at the next one!

2.  Even though not many people showed for this one, the vibe was
great and the people were very nice.  I really enjoyed the
difference from the massives that I've been attending lately.  It
was great to break from the pattern that we've created for ourselves
in that we'd rarely meet new people at raves because we generally go
with a large group of 15 or so friends.

3.  I think that this is an event that is worth supporting and
expanding.

Jen, Steve, and I had a really good time at the New Moon Rave and am
looking forward to the next one - with a few more people attending,
these can be an incredible event.  Mona has some interesting plans
for outdoor spaces that promise to be exciting.

That's all for now, I hope to meet many of you at Friends and Family
this weekend!




- Chris Gilmore
(415-725-8800 days, 408-984-8524 evenings)



PS - John, I didn't read my e-mail after leaving work yesterday, so
did not know that you needed a ride.  If you (or anyone) live in the
South Bay or Peninsula and need a ride to Friends and Family, please
give me a call!


PPS - Paul, you must have been the person who arrived right before
we left.  I'm sorry that I didn't have a chance to meet you as I was
in a pretty deep conversation with Brad.  I hope that we'll meet
sometime soon.

What is the info line number?

vivianm asks.....

>What is phone phreaking?

Ahem!!  And I thought *I* had the bozo award for asking about where
I can get a car window for my Toyota...   Phone Phreaking is the
act of exploring how the telephone network works.    The authorities
frown on these things,  but in the true sense,  it is LEGAL provided
that you don't solicit free phone calls from the system.    Just dialing
up numbers to learn where they take you,  as long as you are not
malicious shouldn't be illegal.   usually while phreaking,  it is 
common that one might discover holes in the system that might allow
for one to make free calls.    But for the most part,   phreaking is
just dialing up numbers,  usually non-standard prefixes,  to see who
is at the other end.   One can find test numbers issuing tones,  and
special computer access numbers for phone company internal use.  Most
of which are useless to the casual phone hacker.   Hope this answers
your question.... From the horses mouth :-)

Saan asks...

>I've read a lot of sympathy for him. What did he do? Was it a
>consentual crime? I hate seeing people imprisoned for these. Was he a
>big community figure?

Phiber was a phone/computer hacker busted by the new NY computer law,
and was one of the first cases prosicuted under this new law.    People
say that he was made an example of (Similar to what happend to me about
20 yrs ago).

CC

From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan 12 14:34:14 1994
From: jamiel@sybase.com (Healthier, More Manageable Hair)
Date: Wed, 12 Jan 1994 14:37:19 -0800
Subject: Re: Phiber Optik
Status: 

At  4:37 PM 1/12/94 -0500, Sean Casey wrote:
>I've read a lot of sympathy for him. What did he do? Was it a
>consentual crime? I hate seeing people imprisoned for these. Was he a
>big community figure?

Phiber Optik was/is a phone phreaker- someone who explores/abuses
(depending on your viewpoint) the phone system. There are ways to redirect
services, tap services that are usually only available to telephone tech
crews, get free calls, etc. if you can figure it out. (Now a lot of this is
computer aided, and so it crosses into cracking, too.) Phiber Optik gained
a pretty big rep as being damn good- he is a big part of the 2600 scene (a
magazine/club into phreaking and computer hacking and the like), and is
very respected in those circles. He was busted for phreaking, pleaded
guilty (they had him pretty well, from what I hear), and in now in jail for
it. A big community figure, and *really* smart and (sorta) likeable. The
case got to be big news, mostly because of him. It just highlights a lot of
controversy around people who know too much about telephony and computers
getting in trouble for it. So no, it wasn't exactly consentual ;).
check out the alt.2600 newsgroup for more info.

>Sean

jamie

From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan 12 16:16:09 1994
From: csc@pilot.njin.net (Sean Casey)
Date: Wed, 12 Jan 94 19:15:59 EST
Subject: ???
Status: 

Busted for phreaking? Let's say I am unfamiliar with the term. Would
that be a euphemism for, say, gaining administrative privileges on the
phone network? Perhaps theft of services, too? Perhaps non-invasive
yet unauthorized network switching?

I've been a hacker and been around many hackers and crackers in my
time. One or two got busted even.  It was pretty much understood that
they didn't want you breaking in, you knew they didn't want you in,
and they knew you knew. If you got caught, you got busted. Those were
the rules of the game; we didn't pretend we were justified in breaking
in if it was "in search of knowledge". We hungered for forbidden
knowledge, and we enjoyed the thrill, and we knew the price of
carelessness.

A lot of people view their systems the same way they view their homes.
If you walk in or break in--harmless or not--uninvited, you're
committing a serious trespass. Whether or not it's an appropriate
analogy, they feel that way. We *should* be exercising the Golden Rule
here.

No, I don't think he should have gone to prison. There are too many
murderers, robbers, rapists, and wife beaters still enjoying their
freedom while Mark sits in a cell. Perhaps some strong measures were
in order, but prison? No. A whole hell of a lot of community service
would have been much better. And God knows I have no love for The
Phone Company.

But I don't think Mark should be completely exonerated. He broke in,
and encouraged a lot of others to do same. He deserves our sympathy
for his cruel punishment, but not for what he has done.

Sean

Subject: sf trip...
Date: Thu, 06 Jan 94 11:18:43 -0800
From: Andrew Thomas <athomas@hydra.acs.uci.edu>


I've been back in socal a couple days now so here's my belated SF trip
report:

Got in tues. (28th) night somewhat excited about checking the FMR.
After getting the location around 12:30 and finding out that it was an
hours drive from the city and wouldn't be starting until 2 I started
having second thoughts, mostly cuz the friend I was staying with had
to go to work the next morning.  It was unfortunate to find out that
it didn't happen but I was relieved that we didn't go.

Thurs. night dana and I headed over to Spacelab.  The music varried between
very good and obnoxious, some of it was a little too stomping for my
tastes but there was also some really good acidy stuff.  It's a
bargain for $3, and it was fun hanging out and meeting new sfravers.

It was difficult figuring out what to do for new years since there was
so much going on.  We were going to head over to mission rock but
ended up going to wicked cuz some other friends were going.  Since
we arived early it was $20 instead of $25 (still pretty steep, I heard
it was only going to be $15), but it was worth it to me.  The location
was amazing, a large parking lot under a freeway downtown.  There was
also a 3 or 4 level building that had another dance floor as well as a
chill room.  The only real compaint (besides the cost) was that is was
really cold outside, especially in the morning.  Most didn't seem to
mind though.  Also the security at times seemed a little rough, at one
point when everybody rushed the fence a girl who was climbing the
inner fence was either pushed really hard or hit by one of the
security guards about 10 feet away from us, this brought the vibe way
down for a while.

The music got really good after midnight.  I'm not sure who the dj was
but I recognized him from Tweekin' (Gavin?), his set was really good.
I also enjoyed Garths set, althogh it wasn't as good as when he came
down to Irvine a couple weeks ago :) Jeno was good but at times
it was getting too vocally for my tastes.  I'm not sure who the other
dj's were but things got really crazy around dawn and the view of the
city was amazing, we headed home around 8ish and it was still going
off pretty hard.  I wish I could've caught Dub Tribe though, I didn't
know when they were going to play and the line to get inside was
long...

The rest of the trip was mostly spent relaxing and record shopping.
Tweekin had a pretty good selection as well as Primal.  Also recently
reopened Record Rack in the castro had a pretty decent import
selection, they mostly carry pop-house and disco, but I found Sabres
of Paradise's Smokebelch II 12" (which I've been looking for) as well
as FSOL's Papau New Guinea and a couple others.  I picked up a lot of
used vinyl at streetlight, they've got a good used cd selection too (a
friend picked up YMO's technodon II (orb remixes) and the Space
Bootleg ($4!) in the bargain bin and some other great stuff) Also
there were about 15 vapour space promo 12"s on FFRR for $1.98, grab it
if you haven't.

It was a great trip, I hope to return soon...

Andy

SF for ?, New york for house+hardcore will be a good choice :-)
but no limitation...
We, European would understand more about US scene, so, explain us!!
