Hi folks,

We've finalized the line-up for the Choc-Lit Factory which will have it's
grand opening on Friday, January 14.  The magic starts at Midnight!

12:00 to 1:30- Masa
1:30 to 3:00  - Dervish
3:00 to 4:30  - DUBTRIBE
4:30 to 6:00  - Bryan Lyons
6:00 to ???   - Spun

The Choc-Lit Factory is a Seattle House Community Cooperative effort to
help save the Velvet Elvis Theater.  Depending on how this show goes, it
will be a weekly event featuring rotating DJ 's, changing themes with 
local visual artists showcased each week.  Our main goal is to creatively
challenge the Seattle House Community by promoting participation, creative
ideas and communication.  

I would like to invite sfravers and nwravers who might be in Seattle in the
future to contact me and participate in our efforts to cultivate our
community.  As the song goes..."My house is your house and your house is
mine....".
Please call (206)323-4304

Peace, Love and Understanding!

Tigger

From sfraves-owner  Thu Jan 13 14:09:44 1994
From: "David M. Ilstrup" <dmi@holonet.net>
Date: Thu, 13 Jan 94 14:05:56 PST
Subject: Phiber out
Status: 


Well, let me start by saying I basicly agree with Dana's point that this
probably doesn't *really* belong on sfr. But...

If any of you are interested in a characterization of Phiber along with
alot of good observations and information about the larger social and legal
issues surrounding the use of and access to networks, like the one/s carrying
sfraves, check out an article by John Barlow in an old CPSR Newsletter.
It's in volume 8, no. 4 (fall 1990) and is called "Crime and Puzzlement".
It's old, but very well written. I've given this to friends whenever they
ask "What the hell do you do with internet?", and the like. If you're
interested, email me; I think I can get the ascii version somewhere.

Keep dancing!

-Dave


From sfraves-owner  Thu Jan 13 14:31:14 1994
From: crunch@netcom.com (John Draper)

Subject: Have new records - wanna spin!!
Status: 


Hi,  I'm about halfway through reviewing the records I got from this
UK record company called Irdial-Discs.    WOW!!  I'm really impressed
with the variaty of records.    Origionally I thought there were 10 
discs,   but learned there were more,  as some of the jackets have
2 disks in them.    Some are very "Housey",   120 BPM stuff,  others
up to about 155 BPM,  but most are around the 135 BPM range. 

As I am reviewing them,  I'm labeling the BPM's on each cut to make 
it easier for the DJ to select the appropriate cuts on the records.

It is my plan to bring them to the Friends and Family party on Sat
evening and spin them (Or have someone else spin them).

All this is new and refreshing stuff.   so look forward to hearing
and dancing to some new and refreshing sounds on Sat evening.

To all interested in the New Moon Raves:


I spoke to Mona (the coordinator of the New Moon Raves) today, and
told her of the interest among the Net regarding these raves.
So, instead of putting out her home phone number (too much traffic!)
she has listed the name and contact number for the NMR's in
a community newspaper called the "Great Day News".  But, I promised
her that I would post it here, for all of you crazy SF ravers!  So,
enjoy, and I hope to meet you -- either on Saturday @ 'Friends &
Family', at the next New Moon, or at any other rave!!
The information number is 415-267-3076.

Take care,


Jennifer   (GC.JXS@FORSYTHE.STANFORD.EDU  OR  415-723-4082)

The following is an advertisement from Nitty Gritty Productions
(Hell, everyone else does one, why not me as well.....)

===============================================================

Nitty Gritty Video's latest release entitled "Let Your Backbone Slide" is
an underground interpretation into the unforgettable house subculture of
SF, and the Bay Area between the years 1991 and 1993.

The video encompasses footage from Toontown, Full Moon Massive, Gathering,
Bulletproof Boat Parties, The Late Train, and 40 other events, all of which
can be seen on this limited release 45 min. video.

Music on the video was provided courtesy of DJ's: Ernie Munson, Garth, and
Gavan.

If you are interested in purchasing a copy of this video, please contact:
Nitty Gritty Video @ (415) 553-8130.

Also available is a live video of The ORB Show at the Warfield on October
15, 1993.  This in-depth video includes a soundcheck and the entire 2 hour
show.

If interested please contact Nitty Gritty Productions @ the number above.

Sincerely,
NGV

When people read your posts you DO kinda come off as a know it all (even

From bbehlen  Fri Jan 14 08:27:12 1994

Subject: Yet another forward (due to non-standard mailers)

Here's another forwarded post - Scott, change your From: address if at all
possible so that your full email address is there.

>From drenalin@duckmail.uoregon.edu  Fri Jan 14 02:21:38 1994
Date: Fri, 14 Jan 1994 02:21:28 -0800 (PST)
From: Scott Michael Nelson <drenalin@duckmail>
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU

This is my first post so please don't harsh on it to much.  My friends 
and I have been raving for about two years now.  I'm going to U. of 
Oregon at the moment but one of my goals recently has been to help the 
rave scene in some way.  Information distribution is the way that I think 
the rave scene could start to change.  At a rave called the Promised Land 
I received a flyer called House Music and Planetary Healing, alot of you 
may have read this flyer.  It was an inspiration to me but is the only 
such flyer I have received in two years!!!!!

This is an idea for a flyer I would like to print up myself in a small 
number to help promote a sort of cleansing and unity in some aspects of 
raving.  I would appreciate it if you have any comments or constructive 
criticism to reply.  Maybe this can become a place where people can 
present some information or an opinion and receive comments and then 
print it up for all of the people that are not on SFRaves that we still 
need to reach.

---------------------------------------

A Higher Consciousness through Dancing

	Take this time to reexamine your role in this underground scene.  
Raves have the potential to be a channeling force for positive ideas and 
the goodness that can bring about change in our society.  To be a 
positive force we must show everyone that we have good intentions for the 
whole of the world and those who live here.  Although drugs can help you 
enter into an altered world or a completely different one there is a 
realm we can all explore inside of ourselves.  I myself have reached 
higher levels of awareness using drugs and am not condemning their use.  
But recently I have been exploring the levels of energy and higher states 
of consciousness that can be reached through dancing with a positve group 
of people while sober.  By dancing with a group of open and positive 
people you can open up your mind and reach a higher plane through 
yourself.  If you have explored this natural high hopefully you can agree 
that it is one of the best and it's free, it's you!!!  I'm tired of 
hearing friends and others saying how they need drugs when they are at a 
rave.  Show yourself and the world that raving is a state of mind that we 
can hold everyday and everywhere to promote unity, peace, and love 
through ourselves and our actions and not through drugs.  Educate 
yourself and others about the joy of life!

---------------------------------

Please reply with any comments and especially any criticism because I'm 
not exactly sure this sounds like I mean it to be and maybe you can help 
me clean up the wording.


The Cloud Factory
---------------------------------------------------------------
!  DJ Adrenalin - The Madlander - DJ Doctor Goto - Tiny Tim   !
! 	Dancing to reach a higher consciousness...	      !
--------------------------------------------------------------


P.S. I have an active (408) voice mail through January maybe February if 
you need a short term line for a rave you're throwing e-mail me and you 
can use it fro a week or two.

Spread the Peace!

From sfraves-owner  Fri Jan 14 10:14:06 1994
From: DWATANAB@uci.edu (Dana Watanabe)
Date: Fri, 14 Jan 94 10:13:49 PST
Subject: Riot Grrrls (ie more silly non-rave related stuff)
Status: 

<wierd psycho comic with a kinda funny pun deleted>

> P.S.  What are "Riot Grrrls", and do they actually exist?

Now thats a good question.
the "Riot Grrrl" movement (?) trend  whatever came out of
the Garage Punk sound that was basically punk with a real poppy sound
and also tended to have females as lead singers
and that more or less came out of more poppy all women bands like
the go-gos or the bangle or tons of others

the label was basically given to bands with women who had dropped
the poppy sound and went for a harder edge to it
and also tended to deal a lot with women's issues
or try to reconstruct the idea of woman through
their performances and lyrics
(esp. through claiming a sexual autonomy or being the 
agressor in the sexual relationship as well as 
reclaiming their bodies: who looks at them and in what ways)

for example: when i was doing sound at a bar for concerts, 
Bikini Kill played there, and me and my male partner were told
"Don't make any sexist comments, they'll beat you up.
If they get hot, they might take off their shirts,
Don't stare at them if they do, they'll beat you up.
etc. etc. etc."

I think that is some of the image that gets portrayed about Riot Grrrl bands
just like it does about other feminists,
and like with other feminists, it was totally false
they were wonderfully nice people, who although could most definitely
do me lots of physical harm, i highly doubt would

BUT apparently, some of the men in the front row of the concert
felt very uncomfortable because while performing them group members
esp. the lead singer, would just look at them in ways
that just basically made them feel very uncomfortable

images that have been popularized have been things like
when L7 dropped their pants in the middle of a concert,
Inger Lore, formerly of the Nymphs, urinated on teh desk
of someone at her label and also in concert said
"My voice is really messed up right now,
so im going to show you how nice girls clear their throats"
and then had her b/f come up on stage and performed oral sex on him
(which also got her arrested)

K Records up in Olympia, WA has been one label that has put out a lot
of stuff by Riot Grrrl bands and solo acts
Theres another label that has come out with lots of stuff whose name
slips my mind right now

personally, i think its one of the only interesting things going
on in the rock scene right now, but its also pretty damn
trendy so there are more and more groups that are 
imitating it without havign the same political motivation

 ,
dana

ALL this info is just what i happen to be coming up with right now
and could be totally wrong, so please correct me if it needs to be done

acid/trance DJs around here (and I agree with this entirely) is that
they just aren't very good DJs.  very little skill in the beat
matching and energy directing departments.  say what you want about
Jeno - the guy can mix and knows how to build a set.  so far, all the
trance DJs i've heard have been flailing blindly through a crate of
aphex twin and black dog 12 inchers.  last night at spacelab was a
textbook example - shoban launched with a *brilliant* Eat Static track
(played about 8% too fast but that's just my opinion) and then utterly
failed to follow up on the promise of that track... energy went
through the floor.  dance area cleared in ten minutes.

From sfraves-owner  Fri Jan 14 10:28:13 1994
From: DWATANAB@uci.edu (Dana Watanabe)

>     I have noticed that most of the music and people you guys "rave"
*ahem* and gals :) :) 

> (every bit of that pun intended) about are acid whatever and smaller
> DJ's. do any of you like house music? and bigger DJ's like ernie munson?

_I_ think that most of the people who are pretty vocal on the list
are pretty burnt out on most large scale events that have a an
amazing lack of creativity and real drive recently

that while they would admit that a lot of the big name DJ's are good,
and like their music, that they are also starting be less creative
and are getting into a rut musically,

the less plastered (on flyers) DJ's tend to vary their musical selection
more and get more daring with the stuff they will play
(i would hazard to guess that this is because more well known
DJ's feel that they have to play a certain thing to make people happy)
(okay, actually im saying that because i've heard that said like
2,000,000 times by really popular DJ's)

and the people who post a lot are also more into the musical creation
side than your average person and are more into making pretty
deep complex music, which _I_believe_ acid is, while house music
is more poppy, and fun oriented 

i think the major reason for the leaning of discussion on this list
is due to the fact that some people post a lot and have a certain leaning
and other people would chime in if the leaning were different
but its not, so they dont

 ,
dana

America today.  I would have never even checked them out if it weren't
for congress and various "Traditional Values" groups freaking out over 
them.  Gee, they must be doing *something* right, I thought.  At first, 
I wasn't sure why I liked them.  But now I think I figured out: The 
Beavis and Buttheads of today are the ravers of tomorrow!

In the world of Beavis & Butthead, things are either "cool", or they
"suck".  Their criteria for what's cool and what sucks represent the
fairly typical twisted outlook of 15 year old socially outcast
white male suburbanites.  Niether jocks nor geeks, they belong to
no clique, and are loyal only to their own interests - adolescent
fascination with sex, money, mischevious destructiveness, catching
a buzz, shirking responsibility, and poking fun at every "respectable"
institution they come into contact with.  Their complete absorption
into their own values and total rejection of more socially accepted ones
seems to have resulted in the perpetuation of their intellectually
and emotionally arrested development (i.e. they are both morons and
jerks).  Ultimately, it is apparent that their extreme idiocy is merely
a reflection of the idiocy of everything they have so far been exposed
to.
 
Beavis & Butthead - Future ravers?  Yes, I think so, and here's why.
 
- Love of music.  Although their taste leans towards metal, I've seen
them boogie to Madonna as well.  They like to dance.  It is pretty
obvious that music that speaks to their emotions is one of the only
positive pleasures in their lives.
 
- Lack of community/family.  It is those who are most lacking in this
area who are most likely to seek it outside the normal structures.
And although it may not be apparent, these guys want to be loved as
much as any of us.
 
- Active Renegades.  Whether it's breaking into a nudist camp, egging
a neighbors house, or holding a neighborhood kid for ransom...B&B seek
fun irregardless of rules or laws.  Their lack of dedication to anything
(too stupid to do anything that well) prevents them from being
truly malicious.  Even the rather heinous acts of blowing up a frog
comes more from boredom than the desire to torture and hurt.  Raving
would satisfy their rebellious spirit and rechannel their destructive
energies.
 
- Disrespect for Leaders.  They march to their own drummer, and all
public figures, even rock stars who are "cool" are targets of ridicule.
B&B will not be led into corporate-approved conformity.  They don't
even have fashion sense.
 
- Transcendental Cowboys.  These guys really want to get high.  They
checked themselves into an emergency room in the hope of getting
prescriptions for cold medicine that would cause "hallucinations", and
Beavis sucked on a frog/toad in an attempt to catch an "awesome buzz".
 
So in conclusion, B&B seem to be fucked up amoralists only because their
society hasn't addressed any of their needs.  They seek many of the
of intense thrills that raving might provide.  While it is true that they
lack the "vibe", and respect for their fellow beings and the environment,
this is only because of their current outcast status and resultant
repressed anger.  Let's not forget that many ravers today have come from
punk/metal/goth/industrial backgrounds.    
 
I could go on about how B&B are really a satire of society and of
themselves (like The Simpsons) and how their "cool" vs "sucks" value
system makes a mockery of all purveyors of "right" and "wrong" and
therefore promotes transcendence from the ego-based absolutists who
would decide for others how people should behave.  Raving is about
freedom and Beavis and Butthead, like information, just want to be free.
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
Lee Fogel/\/\/\/\/\eVerything/\Is/\possiBlE/\/\/\/\/\lxfogel@srv.pacbell.com
____________________________________________________________________________

From sfraves-owner  Sat Jan 15 00:29:26 1994
From: phred@well.sf.ca.us (Fred Heutte)
Date: Sat, 15 Jan 1994 00:29:10 -0800
Subject: Re: Beavis and Butthead go raving
Status: 

That was *cool*, Lee.  Most of the pundit viewpoints I've seen on
Beavis and Butthead *suck*.

Actually, I think Mike Judge and the other B&B crew capture certain
social and behavioral nuanaces dead-on.  Especially in the way that
people portrayed on the show drop their social masks and show who
they really are.  The health inspector who thinks the french-fried
earthworms B&B cooked up to gross out the customers are actually pretty
good, as he walks away from the totally trashed-out burger barn.  The
too-sensitive high school teacher with the ponytail and sensitivity
training who finally applies good old authoritarian tones when B&B get
out of hand.  B&B are the innocents of an in-between era, and while they
are definitely portrayed as *cool*, there is no sugar-coating of their
selfish, inane, ill-informed, hormone-driven behavior.  

So I think the analysis of B&B as future ravers is dead-on too.  
Although at first they would probably take off their shirts, head for
the nearest beer vendors, and start sucking down balloons as fast
as they could be served up!

Ah yes, I can see it now: 'Moby's *cool*.'  'No, Moby *sucks*.'

Heh . . .

I'm really glad to see that the American Rave scene is not as Drug oriented as
I thought it was... In Sweden, many raves are legal, which has it's upsides
and downsides: The upsides are: No cops to bust you at 3 am, GREAT sound and
visuals ( One rave I went to was sponsored by Sanyo, AWESOME!) and not as amny
drugs circulating. The downsides: "Wrong" crowd shows up (peopl who go to pick
fights or just stand around looking bored...) and not as friendly atmosphere
due to cops astnading around watching your every move...

Raving is a state of mind, to some even a religious experience, It should not
be an excuse for people to chemically alter their conciousness. To all fellow
ravers who think that they CANNOT enjoy a rave without E, poppers, nitrous or
whatever: Go sober and enjoy the ULTIMATE high, the NATURAL high, the
ADRENALINE HIGH, the LOVE high, or whatever it is that you might experience,
It's all about being who you are.

We are the future

Right ON! I must say, having been on both sides of the fence that I totally
agree, in fact I was sober for the majority of parties that I went to in 1993.
This was for several reasons:

	1) I don't put random stuff that I don't know what it is 
	in my body and MOSTLY the stuff available was not what it was
	advertised to be.

	2) I wanted to see if there was anything to the experience without
	the aid of xhemical assistance.

	3) At many renegades, I often get to be the one to talk to the 
	authorities and I never talk to them while under the influence.

	4) I was having some incredible deep psychic experiences without
	the chemicals.

I'm not saying don't take substances when you go out.  I've found that 
taking various things can definately get you to a certain place very quickly,
like training wheels on a bicycle, but eventually they hold you back if
you keep using them ALL the time.

These days, I`ll take things at a party as a treat.  If I'm sure the cops
aren't comming and I don't have to work and there are a lot of my friends
around, etc I'll as jsl says, crack-on, but most of the time I get pretty out
there with just myself, although sometimes I must admit, that these days,
all I seem to need to send me through the roof is just a whiff of some good
herb :) Which is something I wouldn't touch 2 years ago. 
I guess I'm just gettin old.

From sfraves-owner  Sat Jan 15 10:26:00 1994

On Fri, 14 Jan 1994, Lee Fogel wrote:

> Date: Fri, 14 Jan 94 12:32:54 PST
> From: Lee Fogel <lxfogel@srv.pacbell.com>
> To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU

> Subject: Re: Beavis and Butthead go raving
> 
> > MykL:  it's amazing what passes for humor in the age of Beavis 
> > and Butthead, huh? 
> 
> ALthough I don't watch much TV, I've recently come to the conclusion
> that Beavis & Butthead are the most important media personalities in
> America today.  I would have never even checked them out if it weren't
> for congress and various "Traditional Values" groups freaking out over 
> them.  Gee, they must be doing *something* right, I thought.  At first, 
> I wasn't sure why I liked them.  But now I think I figured out: The 
> Beavis and Buttheads of today are the ravers of tomorrow!
> 
> In the world of Beavis & Butthead, things are either "cool", or they
> "suck".  Their criteria for what's cool and what sucks represent the
> fairly typical twisted outlook of 15 year old socially outcast
> white male suburbanites.  Niether jocks nor geeks, they belong to
> no clique, and are loyal only to their own interests - adolescent
> fascination with sex, money, mischevious destructiveness, catching
> a buzz, shirking responsibility, and poking fun at every "respectable"
> institution they come into contact with.  Their complete absorption
> into their own values and total rejection of more socially accepted ones
> seems to have resulted in the perpetuation of their intellectually
> and emotionally arrested development (i.e. they are both morons and
> jerks).  Ultimately, it is apparent that their extreme idiocy is merely
> a reflection of the idiocy of everything they have so far been exposed
> to.

So although you say that they are absorbed in their own values not socially
accepted ones, you admit that the values that they have absorbed (their
idiocy) reflects the idiocy of everything they have so far been exposed
to, ie society.  It seems a contradiction in terms.  (Clarify and I'll be
more than happy to agree with you).

Although I agree with your basic premise, I disagree that they are
unintentionally stupid.  Butt-head, especially, shows signs of
intelligence.  Both are grotesquely creative (who would think of playing
frog-baseball or buying a lawn mower with $500.00 or fishing outside a
window) but eccentricly so.  They are by all practical social purposes
"mad" although they make absolute sense in their own minds and in the
minds of the viewers who judge them only by their own internal laws, not
those dictated by society.  These internal laws essentially being no laws
at all. 

Essentially, then, they are polar opposites to society.  Their madness
reflects the same madness of society turned inside out.  We, the viewers,
stand in the middle, the objective sane observers, who identify with the
madness of B&B and with the madness of society.  Both madnesses lie
within: the insanity of the individual in the insanity of the world. 
Almost existential.

> Beavis & Butthead - Future ravers?  Yes, I think so, and here's why.

Oh yes.  I agree here too.  I was a heavy metal head during my teen years
and evolved from AC/DC to Duran Duran to the Cure to Rave.  But I'm not
stupid (to my knowledge). (:

That's all folks
TMS

> area who are most likely to seek it outside the normal structures.
> And although it may not be apparent, these guys want to be loved as
> much as any of us.
>  
> - Active Renegades.  Whether it's breaking into a nudist camp, egging
> a neighbors house, or holding a neighborhood kid for ransom...B&B seek
> fun irregardless of rules or laws.  Their lack of dedication to anything
> (too stupid to do anything that well) prevents them from being
> truly malicious.  Even the rather heinous acts of blowing up a frog
> comes more from boredom than the desire to torture and hurt.  Raving
> would satisfy their rebellious spirit and rechannel their destructive
> energies.
>  
> - Disrespect for Leaders.  They march to their own drummer, and all
> public figures, even rock stars who are "cool" are targets of ridicule.
> B&B will not be led into corporate-approved conformity.  They don't
> even have fashion sense.
>  
> - Transcendental Cowboys.  These guys really want to get high.  They
> checked themselves into an emergency room in the hope of getting
> prescriptions for cold medicine that would cause "hallucinations", and
> Beavis sucked on a frog/toad in an attempt to catch an "awesome buzz".
>  
> So in conclusion, B&B seem to be fucked up amoralists only because their
> society hasn't addressed any of their needs.  They seek many of the
> of intense thrills that raving might provide.  While it is true that they
> lack the "vibe", and respect for their fellow beings and the environment,
> this is only because of their current outcast status and resultant
> repressed anger.  Let's not forget that many ravers today have come from
> punk/metal/goth/industrial backgrounds.    
>  
> I could go on about how B&B are really a satire of society and of
> themselves (like The Simpsons) and how their "cool" vs "sucks" value
> system makes a mockery of all purveyors of "right" and "wrong" and
> therefore promotes transcendence from the ego-based absolutists who
> would decide for others how people should behave.  Raving is about
> freedom and Beavis and Butthead, like information, just want to be free.
> ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~

> > MykL:  it's amazing what passes for humor in the age of Beavis 
> > and Butthead, huh? 
> 
> ALthough I don't watch much TV, I've recently come to the conclusion
> that Beavis & Butthead are the most important media personalities in
> America today.  I would have never even checked them out if it weren't
> for congress and various "Traditional Values" groups freaking out over 
> them.  Gee, they must be doing *something* right, I thought.  At first, 
> I wasn't sure why I liked them.  But now I think I figured out: The 
> Beavis and Buttheads of today are the ravers of tomorrow!
> 
> In the world of Beavis & Butthead, things are either "cool", or they
> "suck".  Their criteria for what's cool and what sucks represent the
> fairly typical twisted outlook of 15 year old socially outcast
> white male suburbanites.  Niether jocks nor geeks, they belong to
> no clique, and are loyal only to their own interests - adolescent
> fascination with sex, money, mischevious destructiveness, catching
> a buzz, shirking responsibility, and poking fun at every "respectable"
> institution they come into contact with.  Their complete absorption
> into their own values and total rejection of more socially accepted ones
> seems to have resulted in the perpetuation of their intellectually
> and emotionally arrested development (i.e. they are both morons and
> jerks).  Ultimately, it is apparent that their extreme idiocy is merely
> a reflection of the idiocy of everything they have so far been exposed
> to.

So although you say that they are absorbed in their own values not socially
accepted ones, you admit that the values that they have absorbed (their
idiocy) reflects the idiocy of everything they have so far been exposed
to, ie society.  It seems a contradiction in terms.  (Clarify and I'll be
more than happy to agree with you).

Although I agree with your basic premise, I disagree that they are
unintentionally stupid.  Butt-head, especially, shows signs of
intelligence.  Both are grotesquely creative (who would think of playing
frog-baseball or buying a lawn mower with $500.00 or fishing outside a
window) but eccentricly so.  They are by all practical social purposes
"mad" although they make absolute sense in their own minds and in the
minds of the viewers who judge them only by their own internal laws, not
those dictated by society.  These internal laws essentially being no laws
at all. 

Essentially, then, they are polar opposites to society.  Their madness
reflects the same madness of society turned inside out.  We, the viewers,
stand in the middle, the objective sane observers, who identify with the
madness of B&B and with the madness of society.  Both madnesses lie
within: the insanity of the individual in the insanity of the world. 
Almost existential.

> Beavis & Butthead - Future ravers?  Yes, I think so, and here's why.

Oh yes.  I agree here too.  I was a heavy metal head during my teen years
and evolved from AC/DC to Duran Duran to the Cure to Rave.  But I'm not
stupid (to my knowledge). (:

That's all folks
TMS

From sfraves-owner  Sat Jan 15 15:34:10 1994
From: alves@bethe.ucdavis.edu (David Alves)
Date: Fri, 14 Jan 94 15:18:41 PST
Subject: very itchy

Apparently I was hallucinating the other night at 4 am which my wife
thought was pretty funny.  I did go to the doctor the next day.

Phone Phreaking, Riot Grrls, Beavis and Butthead ...

All this pop culture discussion reminded me of an essay I started a 
a few months ago.  Here is the first chapter (don't worry, it is short)
Hope you like it!


**********************




		Fuedal Anarchy and Pedagogic Existentialism
		   The Beavis and Butthead Connection
	
				   by

		    Jean-Paul Sartre and David Alves 
				



**********************

Chapter One:	  Anguish, Beavis says "Pole"


	First, what is meant by anguish?  The existentialists say at once that
man is anguish.  What this means is this: the man who involves himself and who
realizes that he is not only the person he chooses to be, but also a lawmaker
who is, at the same time, choosing all mankind as well as himself, can not
help escape the feeling of his total and deep responsibility.  Of course,
there are many people who are not anxious; but we claim that they are hiding
their anxiety, that they are fleeing from it.  Certainly, many people believe
that when they do something, they themsleves are the only ones involved, and
when someone says to them, "What if everyone acted that way?" they shrug their
shoulders and answer, "Everyone doesn't act that way."  But really, one should
always ask himself, "What would happen if everybody looked at things that way?"
There is no escaping this disturbing thought except by a kind of double-
dealing.  A man who lies and makes excuses for himself by saying that "not 
everybody does that," is someone with an uneasy conscience, because the act of 
lying implies that a universal value is conferred upon the lie.


	Anguish is evident even when it conceals itself.  This is the anguish
Keirkegaard called the anguish of Abraham.  As it is so painfully obvious to
the viewers of Beavis and Butthead yet concealed from the characters within
the context of their world, we are witness to profound anguish.  Why does
Beavis find humor in the hardening of his penis if it is not the denial of,
or more benevolently, the profound understanding of the very paradox that 
modern man must face.  The analogy is striking.  I have penis therefore I am.
Butthead is forced to question, "Do I have a penis?  How do I know?  What
proof do I have?"  What proof indeed!  Is the momentary state of his penis
a pathological condition or his conscious choice for man?  For every man,
everything happens as if all mankind had its eyes fixed on him and were guiding
itself by what he does.  There is no question here of the kind of anguish
which would lead to quietism, to inaction.


**********************

Chapter Two:	Heidegger's Forlornness, The Trailer Park Episode

(haven't done it yet)

**********************

From sfraves-owner  Sat Jan 15 16:47:57 1994
From: winston@lurnix.COM (Mark Guthrie)
Date: Sat, 15 Jan 94 14:46:24 PST
Subject: Re: Rave &drugs
Status: 

 I know of
some states of mind that all but the most enlightened can only "think"
about, rather than experience it directly, w/o such sacraments.
-----------------------------------------------------------------

I'd go further and even say that "enlightened" people still can't experience
these states (if they're anything like the ones I've had ;-).  I think it's
drug-culture myth that mystics, yogis, misc. eastern religious acheive the
same or even similar states as psychedelic experiences.  There are 
similarities, I'm sure, but I think it's an overused comparison, and maybe
even a little insulting to the "enlightened" and mis-leading to everyone.
Some similarities are that both methods can give you the feeling of
understanding or comprehension of the universe (and beyond) and the feeling
of "enlightenment" but one way is through meditation and is a calm  
contemplation of reality while the other is a sometimes aggresive roler coaster
ride throught reality (and un-reality, whatever either one of them are).  I
don't think enlightened yogis feel the same feelings and see the same visual
effects or that there minds race at such seemingly high speeds from one thought
to the next or that they feel that intense joy or so overwhelmingly loose
touch with everything.  I know you can get way out there with meditation
because I've done some and I'm sure that a practitoner of 20 yrs. can get
into some interesting states of mind but it's a slow relaxed jouney, where
psychedelics don't even give you the time to pack your suitecase.  I think
they are just opposites that take you to a similar destination.  Meditative
states and enlightenment are more stable too, in that you don't realy have
to all-out "loose" it in order to "find" it.

-Mark

From sfraves-owner  Sat Jan 15 17:46:19 1994
From: mcg@netcom.com (MykL G)
Date: Sat, 15 Jan 1994 17:51:15 -0800
Subject: Re: Well, it's almost been two weeks
Status: 

Via the keyboard of Dana Watanabe:

> and the people who post a lot are also more into the musical creation
> side than your average person and are more into making pretty
> deep complex music, which _I_believe_ acid is, while house music
> is more poppy, and fun oriented.

I personally disagree about acid being more complex.  Most of the acid house
I hear is just little more than a 303 or Super Jupiter doing lots of bloops
and filter sweeps and a 909 hammering away.  House for me has lots more
subtlety and complexity, combining more traditional instruments with
tweaky samples.  And it's usually more rhythmically complex and interesting.

This is especially true of really deep house, which I prefer to the
more commercial "straight" house music where vocals tend to be a bit too
prominent.

I feel a flame war coming on -- I will only respond privately to any
followups on this (if at all)...


--=-=-===-==---=--=-=-==-=-=-=-=-  MykL --=-=----==-=-=----==--==----=--=-

> even a little insulting to the "enlightened" and mis-leading to everyone.
> Some similarities are that both methods can give you the feeling of
> understanding or comprehension of the universe (and beyond) and the feeling
> of "enlightenment" but one way is through meditation and is a calm  
> contemplation of reality while the other is a sometimes aggresive roler coaster
> ride throught reality (and un-reality, whatever either one of them are).  I
> don't think enlightened yogis feel the same feelings and see the same visual
> effects or that there minds race at such seemingly high speeds from one thought
> to the next or that they feel that intense joy or so overwhelmingly loose
> touch with everything.  I know you can get way out there with meditation
> because I've done some and I'm sure that a practitoner of 20 yrs. can get
> into some interesting states of mind but it's a slow relaxed jouney, where
> psychedelics don't even give you the time to pack your suitecase.  I think
> they are just opposites that take you to a similar destination.  Meditative
> states and enlightenment are more stable too, in that you don't realy have
> to all-out "loose" it in order to "find" it.
> 
> -Mark
> 

Well I do think the experiences are different, I won't say that one is 
superior to the other, it's like saying a screw driver is more useful
than a hammer, there are instancs where you will luck out if you have
one or the other, (You'll be in really good shape if you have both,
unless what you really need is a wrench, but we digress :)

I have had profound experience while drunk but don't think drinking
is a "spiritual path" to enlightenment.  Neither are psychedelics,
but they most definately are tools that can be used on the Path.
Just remember what your reasons are for starting the Journey.

Some meditation is calm but not all,  I have been _DEEPLY_ into trance
(one full moon morn at bonnie dune, with Jeno spinning) without imbibing
a single thing, I must say my deepest "Vibe States" have been reached
without psychedelics.  But I have reached some very deep and magical
states with the use of certain things.  I think It would have taken me
longer to get to those states if I had NEVER used psychedelics but
I don't think that you need to use them continueously to continue
to make progress.  I know for me there are times when I take things to
seek enlightenment but there are times when I take things t HAVE FUN.

An experience of Gnosis can occur with or without Psychedelics
(But I must admit it can be more _fun_ with)

From sfraves-owner  Sun Jan 16 20:37:55 1994

Hi, folks!

Many thanks to you all, netters, for helping to make Friends and Family 
*the* best party I've ever been to in my life!  I'm really happy to have
helped with some of the logistics for the party, and some small promotion,
to help get things rolling.  Clearly, though, this was a collective effort
by *everyone* to blast off to another space and time.  The whole party
just felt right, from the very beginning, all the way through to the very
end as I helped unload the sound system.

Many thanks to Steve/Resonate and his housemates for providing a wonderful
space for us all to do the do.  Many thanks for the care they provided in
setting up the space, providing water and munchies, and for acting as the
cleanup crew...bravo!

Many thanks to Ethan for the best sound system...Sound Vision just keeps
getting better and better!  I pat myself on the back for providing part
of the sound system for the upstairs, with a big nod to Steve again for
the sound in the dark chill room, and a prop to Amit for his gear. Live
house for the family...weeee-o!

Major props to all of the DJs!  bitchin' music all night long in both
spaces...chill and dark! Wow! way to move people!  Major props, too, for
everyone of them for providing the space and time for everyone who wanted
to play...truly a remarkable achievement...no ego, only fun.

Special thanks to Philip Chang and (humbly) myself, for getting this all
on DAT, too...we have the recordings to prove it to ourselves, too!

Most of all, the biggest props to every single person who came...smiles
were in effect from the get go, everyone pitched in to *make* the vibe.
Lots of consideration, lots of patience when things got cramped or didn't
go quite as expected.

I was very happy to see everyone who came out...so nice to see you all
after such a long time...it's always a pleasure to get together with you
all.  Sorry to have missed some of you...it was a legendary party, and
I wish you could have been there to share it with us, and I'm sorry that
you had to be elsewhere.  I hope to see you soon!

There's just too many great things that happened for me to recount...
guess you had to be there.  

I can tell you that it was a pleasure, and really easy to load out the
sound systems after this party.  There have been events I've helped
load out from where it was "drag my butt coz it has to be done".  This
was a real high.  It was an honor and a privilege to help provide a few
of the underpinnings for this party.  It was even fun to act as the greeter
for a little bit...it was so much fun to see happy people coming and going!

Wow! is all I can say.  This one set a new standard for me!
--

Subject: Friends & Family aka Blue Cube.
 
Hey, this was a really fun party. The attitude level was way down, and the
relaxation level was way up. The 'cube' itself was a little crowded to dance
in, but that has the advantage of forcing you to talk to the people you're
dancing with :) The wierd part was meeting several people I didn't know
that knew people that I had tried to get to go to the party... actually,
it is a little known fact that there are really only 34 human souls in the
universe, and all the rest is done with mirrors; think about it, have you
ever had more than 34 of your friends in one place at one time? The only
bad part was when someone put the salsa under the faucet and it turned into
red tide. Amit (sp?) did some really well paced 'live' housey ambient, with
keyboard over sequences upstairs. Didn't get to hear Mescalina, but he's
on KALX right now. To everyone involved in pulling this off, Great Job!
If more of these go off, '94 should be great!

From sfraves-owner  Sun Jan 16 23:07:26 1994
From: Seth Joshua Horvitz <acid23@uclink.berkeley.edu>
Date: Sun, 16 Jan 1994 22:37:56 -0800 (PST)
Subject: Re: well, it's almost been two 
Status: 

(MykL says he thinks house is more complex than acid) 
> 
> yay mykl, i was trying to work out a reponse to this bit of bullshit, but not
> being a current active member of the sf scene was hesitant, I KNEW I COULD
> COUNT ON YOU!!  

A lot of people have the impression that "acid" is just 303's and
909's, but I think acid encompasses a lot more than that.  For me, acid
can be used as a description for any song which does something to tweak my
brain.  Although 303's are a perfect tool for this, almost anything can be
used to create an acid-like sound.  Trying to say whether house is more
complex than acid is kind of pointless, like trying to compare two races
of people.  I don't think you can really make such broad generalizations. 
Take, for example, Amorphous Androgynous (something which I very much
consider extremely acidic) versus anything out on Strictly Rhythm records
(straight up house).  No comparson here, Amorphous is about as complex as
they come.  BUT, we could easily compare a really complex house song
(sorry, can't think of one right now- my bias is revealed 8)  to a 303/808
or 303/909 acid house track.  Well, you see where I'm going here...
Basically, the whole argument is pointless.

As far as Maria's comments on SpaceLab, I have to say the crowd this past
Thursday was ESPECIALLY bad, very few people willing to dance, and it is
true that in certain cases the DJ's there fail to lift the crowd up, but
if you were there the week before, you would have felt totally different. 
The place was packed, the energy was high, and there was a great DJ/crowd
connection going on.  The thing I like about SpaceLab is that it's
something DIFFERENT from the rest of SF.  This club has only just started,
so I'm sure they're still working on perfecting everything and getting a
steady, energetic crowd.  Don't give up!  Try again this week!

Just my $0.07

From sfraves-owner  Mon Jan 17 11:37:29 1994
From: brycer@netcom.com (Bryce Ryan)
Date: Mon, 17 Jan 1994 11:35:41 -0800 (PST)
Subject: Re: Sony Headphones
Status: 

My mailer says that Howard Berkey said:
> 
> Anyone else know the difference?
> 
I recently made a comparison of the V6's and V600's.  I found the frequency
response to be radically different between the two.  I personally preferred
the response of the V6's, but other people who made the same comparison
preferred the V600 frequency response.  My personal observation was that
the V600's emphasized the low frequencies (in comparison to the V6's).
I have a high end pair of studio headphones with an incredibly flat response
that I use at home, which is probably why I prefer the V6 response.  I
can understand wanting to have more prominent bass response for DJing house
and techno.  I highly recommend a side by side comparison if one is available.
Although the V6's have been discontinued, I have seen stock in most of the
stereo and electronic shops I've visited in the SF Bay Area in the past
month.  Oh, and importantly, the price seems to be the same for the two
models.
--

From sfraves-owner  Mon Jan 17 15:18:50 1994
From: WILL-E <kia@eden.rutgers.edu>
Date: Mon, 17 Jan 94 17:55:10 EST
Subject: Sony Headphones
Status: 

> The MDR-V600s are identical to the V-6s in every way as far as I can
> tell.  I've used both and I can't tell a difference in style or sound
> quality.

NO! The V6 headphones were discontinued because they were replaced with a new
and better model.  This replacement model is the MDR-7506 *NOT* V600.

Not only is the MDR-7506 model the replacement, but it is an *improvement*
over the old V6 model which is why they discontinued it in the first place.
I bought mine for $82 at Sam Ash in New York city.  Most stores are eager to 
get rid of the old V6 model which explains why they're on sale all over.

Bryce is right, the V600 line has a different frequency response.  You
should compare the 7506 side by side with a pair of V600, the V600 isn't as 
brilliant/clear sounding.

From sfraves-owner  Mon Jan 17 15:51:39 1994

Holy Shit! What a party  :)

First off wanted to thank everyone that helped out, most especially Bryce
without whom this party and many others future and past would never have
come off. Analog, *the* coolest guy and most gracious host I've ever
encountered. Sean Casey and Gregor Moshe for lots of hard work setting up
and tearing down. And of course *you* for being there with all your smiles
and positive energy. I really feel like we opened up a hole in the
space/time fabric on this one, really warped  ;) And lets not forget the
neighbors. Heard one woke up in the morning and said: "Martha, I had the
strangest dream last night..."  ;-)

Not enough said about the music so-far:

Derek: great jazzy set really got me feeling warm and fuzzy, all smiles.

Giamma: Kinda blew my mind matching beats on his Denon, makes it look easy.
Really excellent music too, very soulful housy stuff with lots of energy.

Me: thought it went allright; I don't usually spin house, but I was in the
mood and it seemed to go over ok. Lot of the music I played was fresh out
of the shrink wrap, so I look forward to working with it a bit more.

Jon D.: Jon was in a different dimension, one of the best sets I've ever
heard. I'm at a loss to attach a name to what I heard; kinda housy, trancy,
acidic, percussive, mind bending shit. 

Laura: Ditto. Laura really did the do. Flawless trancy/acidic set, really
worked the crowd.

Mescalina: this guy is the Acid King. His music selection was so internally
consistent, every song just worked perfectly with the one before/after.
Really impressed me.

Rocky: First time on the Denon and he smoked too. i had freinds coming up
to me asking who he was and just flipping over his music.

Brad: Spun for an hour early in the morning. Nice housy, trancy stuff. We
were all alittle wrecked by then. Like to here him when he's fresh.

Fred: only caught part of his set, sounded great though. I expect we'll
here more from Fred in the future.

Bryce: unfortunately I missed all of his set cos I was playing. Heard he
wreaked havoc with some twisted european acid though :)

Dr. Teeth: I missed his set too. People I talked to however, went on and
and on about what he was doing. I think getting more live house/trance/acid
etc. into the scene is a definite must.

Jesse: a freind of mine who just coincidentally showed up and spun some
really deep dub upstairs. People really loved it!

DJ Crunch: caught a couple of his famed toons. Mostly stuff on Iridial
(sp?) records. Nice toons. I'm *sure* we'll here more from The Captain. :)

The dijeridoo players: really blew some minds; who are you? step forward
and identify yourselves, we want you :)

Plus many others: lots of folks had fun on the decks, good opportunity for
the ultimate in the DIY experience.

I can hardly wait to hear the tapes :)

Really enthused in the afterglow of this party. In the wake of the last
Liquid Air, I think this list really generated a lot of positive energy and
information about what it takes for us to be a community. Personally, I
consciously tried to integrate that feedback into making this party come
off. While I appreciate all the thanks I have recieved, I did not throw
this party; I consider it a group effort and I think we did a hell of a job
and really want to thank each and every one of you for your feedback,
energy, creativity, and support. 

Looks like a good year ahead.

peace always
ethan

From sfraves-owner  Mon Jan 17 19:05:53 1994
From: resonate@netcom.com (analog resonate)
Date: Mon, 17 Jan 1994 19:06:18 -0800
Subject: @=|====>----
Status: 


	Here's a little story for you.

	There once was a disinterested punk rocker who had a subliminal craving
for electronic music who was, unbeknownst to himself, looking for a scene that
had more to offer his senses than the burned out negative iconographic punk
rock scene. He started working at raves during the breakbeat phase and enjoyed
the crowds and the sci-fi aspects but really didn't the *people* who crowded the
massive gigs like Psychadelic Apocalypse and Mr. Floppys. He worked very hard
to provide quality graphics and interactive computer fun stuff but never found
any rewards outside of being able to get himself and his friends in for free.
He would argue on the internet for hours with a character at Berkeley called
"vitamin B" about the nature of this rave scene but was convinced that it would
only be a consumeristic dead end like punk rock.
	So he took of for a year of travel around the USA working at normal
concert halls and seeing our great and diverse (and bizarre) nation and noticed
something interesting. The "techno" music which used to be horrible noisy 
digital and square-wavy stuff started waning and a much high quality composed
and rich sounding "trance" music started flowing. He also started going to 
smaller and harder to access parties and found them to be a nice scene.
Each city, no matter how small, seemed to be growing an underground dance
scene. In between concert tours he went to SF parties which were by far
the best.
	As the parties he found got to be better and better he started noticing 
something: many of them seemed to feature a smiling two tall goateed guys 
running the sound and talking to everyone. One had tattooed arms and the other
had many piercings. The connection between the good parties and these two 
figures was never lost upon our former-punk rocker who had by then ditched his 
leather jacket and donned his striped shirts. He had many friends like 
caliban, blindman, umlaut etc... who had worked with him on events in Santa Cruz
but SF was new territory.
	In time he tired of travelling around the USA and decided to move to
Japan and work in audio and sound there. He sold off almost everything he owned
and prepared to move until he was snatched out of his plans by an amazing 
digital sound company in Marin. He had planned to eventually move to SF when he
was successful later in life but now SF was to become his home.
	After a few months in SF he came to know the names and faces of the
tall smiling goatee guys and after talking to them realized that their energy
and dreams were very similar to his and that eventually they must work together.
All of our former-punk now ravers' skills were used to show our goatee brothers
his style of event promotion and managment and lo- they energies merged and
two very successful parties were generated: SFR New Years and the Blue Cube 
Friends and Family.
	These are just the very smallest examples of what the future will hold.
To our tall goatted guys- the one with the tattooed arms and the one with the
pierces: my heart goes out to you. And anyone else who wants to join and help
create a place where we can dance and dwell in our own surreal and beat filled
space.
	If you are having a party and want help: i'm *always* on line. always.
More organizers = more events = more family = more organizers ...

			(((((((((((resonate)))))))))))
	
	         Steve Lerner 415-282-6057 resonate@netcom.com

From sfraves-owner  Tue Jan 18 02:03:45 1994
From: turpin@apple.com (johnnymartian)
Date: Tue, 18 Jan 1994 02:04:38 -0800
Subject: A new challenge
Status: 


Hi all, epsecially those who are into sk8'ing...

If anyone should get bored by the simple act of movin one's feet to the
bang of the beat, may I remind you of, or introduce you to the Golden Gate
park Sunday Roller Disco rink. (I know, but I missed all the fun of the
70's disco scene)

Ahh I can see the Beer commercial now... "If you can combine the mentally
stimulating activity of raving, with the sheer physical challenge of
Skating..."

Last Sunday, after attending the Blue Cube party and crashing at Rob&Sin's,
I awoke to a bright and beautiful Sunday morning, went for a stroll up and
down Irving street to find breakfast, and then put on my blades and cruised
over to the park. I had been once last year, but it must have been a bad
day, because unlike last Sunday, I saw very few accomplished skaters.

There were three Hot-Spots I found at the park last Sunday. The first was
the above mentioned disco rink. This was a relatively small oval asphalt
rink with a pretty cheesy boom box setup on one side. Most of the people
skating were relatively talented skaters who could easily dance and skate
at the same time.  I did not percieve an attitude vibe  from these people.
It seemed as though they were happy to have anyone out there who enjoyed
skating and dancing to music. The best scene here was a guy who was jumping
length-wise over a mountain bike. (Ok so this is not dancing, but it
certainly was entertaining to watch). After this got boring, he turned the
bike so that it was perpindicular to his path and then jumped the frame
doing a 360 in the air. Now, I don't consider doing a 360 on skates
terribly difficult, but over a mountain bike... lets just say I'm not sure
if the guy has a full time job.

I wonder if they would mind real DJ's... Hmmm.

Another hot spot was the slalom course. It was really cool watching the
"pros" cruise through the course at high rates of speed. Of course going
forward on two skates was much too easy, they also went forwards on one,
backwards on one, forwards criss crossing each skate, backwards criss
crossing each skate, and my favorite, the
bowlegged-both-skates-pointed-outward slalom (I only saw two guys that
could do this) all at high speeds. Could these have been members of the
Roller Blade professional team? They all knew each others names, and one
guy was actually wearing a "Team Roller Blade" shirt. The guys that I saw
doing this were some of the same guys that were going off at the roller
disco earlier.

The third hot spot were these stairs in front of a white building (it was
kinda like a gift store or something). The same group of guys entertained
themselves, and a crowd of people, as they went flying down these stairs
again and again. Of course once this got easy, they started jumping half
way down the stairs and somehow retaining balance with 10 stairs left to go
down.

Anyway, I am looking for others interested in skating also. I came from a
skating town (skateboarding) and a skateboarding childhood. I progressed to
ramps and half-pipes in college and got pretty comfortable doing simple
grinds and slides on large ramps. I also experimented with street or
freestyle skating, until I broke my ankle doing a 360 boneless off a raised
platform.

I re-kindled my skating spirit last summer and bought a pair of inline
skates and progressed pretty quickly on these, but have only sporadically
given them the time they need for me to become advanced.

So, anyone else out there who wants to skate?  I currently only own inline
skates and not a board, but I may end up getting back into the board stuff
also. I'm interested in anything from leisure Sunday strolls in the park to
aggressive circuit training including speed skating ovals (my personal
favorite), slalom course workouts, and freestyle practice.

If next Sunday is as beautiful as last Sunday, I will be there again
hopefully with much improved balance and more protection (I had none last
Sunday - this was not a good thing especially after the extremely close
call with the speeding biker)


skate   hard
dance   hard
sk8ance hard  :)


johnny t.
turpin@apple.com


Future assignment: To combine Skating, Climbing, and Raving.

From sfraves-owner  Tue Jan 18 05:55:18 1994
From: Tanya Smith <tmsmith@gibbs.oit.unc.edu>
Date: Tue, 18 Jan 1994 08:27:46 +0500 (EST)
Subject: Raves & Drugs
Status: 


> > 
> 
> Well I do think the experiences are different, I won't say that one is 
> superior to the other, it's like saying a screw driver is more useful
> than a hammer, there are instancs where you will luck out if you have
> one or the other, (You'll be in really good shape if you have both,
> unless what you really need is a wrench, but we digress :)

I basically agree with you and Mark, however, I question your analogy.  I
think meditation and psychedelic experiences will perhaps enhance the
quality of life (I am being generous here for my trips have been fun but
have not enhanced my life one bit) but they are not requisite to enjoy a deep
and meaningful life.  

 > 
> I have had profound experience while drunk but don't think drinking
> is a "spiritual path" to enlightenment.  Neither are psychedelics,
> but they most definately are tools that can be used on the Path.
> Just remember what your reasons are for starting the Journey.
> 
> Some meditation is calm but not all,  I have been _DEEPLY_ into trance
> (one full moon morn at bonnie dune, with Jeno spinning) without imbibing
> a single thing, I must say my deepest "Vibe States" have been reached
> without psychedelics.  But I have reached some very deep and magical
> states with the use of certain things.  I think It would have taken me
> longer to get to those states if I had NEVER used psychedelics but
> I don't think that you need to use them continueously to continue
> to make progress.  I know for me there are times when I take things to
> seek enlightenment but there are times when I take things t HAVE FUN.
> 
> An experience of Gnosis can occur with or without Psychedelics
> (But I must admit it can be more _fun_ with)

The last trip I took was almost my final trip.  I almost discovered the
meaning of the universe (it had something to do with second-guessing and
the motivation of events and action).  Nevertheless, when I returned to
planet earth I hadn't the foggiest notion of what that meaning was.  LSD
destroys the ego which lies between the id and superego; when that ego was
put back into place I lost whatever I had gained.
Now, when I am meditating, whether it is on the dancefloor or while
running (exercise helps me accomplish the state), I have no need to figure
out the meaning of the universe; I am the universe.  I am part of the
whole, I AM.  There is extasy in that moment, I enter a state when mind
and body and soul are ALIVE.  And guess what?  When I return to the
isolation of the individual, I REMEMBER it.  I remember what I had gained
because I am permanently altered by the experience.  It has incorporated
itself into my being.  It is not the removal of something (the ego) but
the addition of something (wholeness).
My personal view on psychedelics and meditation.
TMS

first of all id like to give a great big thanks to cindy kawakami for
letting me stay at her place in sf and for picking me up at the airport
and showing me around town - thank you very much! i had a great time!

well, phew- where do i start???? friday i got into sf around 8pm, and
cindy met me  at the gate- from there we drove to twin peaks to look at
the awesome view of the lights, the city and the bay... we then went back
to cindy's place, where i met rob and jeno the cat (a very nutty cat i
must say) - we tried to figure out something to do but there didnt seem to
be too much going on.... there was a renegade that night but the location
(outdoors no less) wasn't announced until like 3:30 - and i was smashed
from the 3 hour difference- so i hung around cindy's for a while then
called susie up and went over to her place in the haight area.... i met
derek chung, ovid and a fellow chris who was staying with susie... we
watched the sf orb show, and the full moon madness tape by the nitty
gritty video folks while waiting for the renegade location to be
announced.... at about 4am i decided that i would have to get some sleep
and i walked back to cindy's place and crashed (susie neglected to tell me
that i'd be walking across the panhandle - the location of most crime in
her area - oh well :) ) 

at 6am i was awoken by the very loud meowing of jeno - and then he somehow
got the door to cindys room open and came in and began meowing in my face
and generally trying to wake me up - i quickly got the cat out of the room 

saturday cindy and i walked around chinatown, went to the golden gate
bridge, and north beach -we went to a couple of used bookstores, ate at a
chow mein place, and generally milled around until she had to be at work -
at which time she dropped me off at susies place where i hung out with
chris.... later on that afternoon susie got back from classes and brian
and laura came over, who i had met fri nite (or was it sat morning- my
chronology is messed up :) ) - and we all hung out until it was time to
get something to eat... after dinner chris and i went to brian and lauras
awesome appartment until it was time to go to the cube.

when we first got to the blue cube there werent that many people there so
i tried to meet the folks that were already there - i met sooo many cool
people there that night - way too many to list - all very freindly
people!! a big shout out to you all! derek was down stairs spinning so i
went down and started dancing.. people started to come in and it started
getting hotter and the energy kept building up.  the sound system wasnt
loud at all at that time, but it has to be one of the cleanest, crispest
sound system ive heard! i'm not quite sure who was spinning when- but i
think it was ethan's set that i really got into, along with jon drukmans
and lauras- phat tunes spun by all this night though!!!!!  by midnight i
think (or maybe i was losing track of time) the downstairs room was just
packed, and hot as a sauna - but i couldnt quit dancing because of all of
the energy and intense music -- i havent seen much quite like this on the
east coast yet.... i liked the black light downstairs- it really made the
sfr banner look incredible, and lauras laser too :)

by 4:30 or so i was beat- still unused to the time difference so i caught
a ride back with brian and laura and a carload of other folks - thank you
brian for going out of your way to drop me back by cindy's!

i must say i had an incredible time in sf this weekend and met soooo many
cool people - i didnt meet as many people at the cube party as i would
have liked to but i was just so overcome by the energy and the nusic i had
to dance!

big thansk go out to resonate for sharing his home with everyone, bryce,
ethan, all the dj's, and everyone who helped w/ friends and family for a
wonderful party, and to everyone there for being so friendly and emanating
a massive vibe for everyone!!!

i had to kind of leave sf abruptly b/c i was worried about getting back to
school for classes- i almost got stuck in charlotte, NC last night b/c of
all the bad weather..... but i will be back, hopefully very soon!

peace out!

greg

Friends and Family at the Blue Cube was the best party I've ever

many people having so much fun.

presence!

:).

chill out room. We had the trip toys ("Oh my God!").

From sfraves-owner  Tue Jan 18 10:42:03 1994
From: lxfogel@srv.PacBell.COM (Lee Fogel)
Date: Tue, 18 Jan 94 10:41:55 PST
Subject: F&F
Status: 

Just wanted to thank Resonate, Ethan, Bryce and everyone else who
helped put this on.  The things that stick out for me were:

- As crowded as the Blue Cube got, I think that the lack of smoke was
the key to keeping the space hospitable.  It's a drag to have to police
people, but I have to give points to Resonate for enforcing this.

- The music was great.  The progression of energy from Ethan
to Jon to Laura really worked for me.  I especially peaked on Laura's
set.  Just the kind of good hard trance that I love, similar to stuff
I've heard Goa Gil play, except that Laura can beat match.  The volume
was a bit low, but that probably kept the party from being busted.
Mescalina played some interesting stuff that was a little dark for
where my head was at, but this just added to the variety that made
the whole evening special.

- Live music.  The keyboard playing in the kitchen and the 
digideroos made this party feel like a real participatory happening.
This is what raving is all about - the party is *us*.

- Infectious vibe.  There were quite a few people who heard about this
party and stopped by on the way to Organic, and stayed.  One house
scene old-timer remarked to me "So this is being put on by your
SFRaver net friends?  What a wonderful party!"  It was great to see 
quite a few people outside the SFR community having a such a good time.

- The people.  I'm not sure how many attended, I would guess 200+.
For such a packed open house party, everyone seemed respectful of
the place and each other.  I have to applaud the lack of alchohol
and the enhanced vibe for some of this, but mostly, it was just a
reflection of just how cool our community is.

- New UVC.  Jon unveiled a preliminary version of the new UVC single.
ALthough it didn't blow me away, it's definately a well crafted, solid 
tune.  No doowop vocals, though.

- leg of eel

meaningless. The only meaningful metric is one's ears. 

The only stat I even bother to look at anymore is "Headphone output
voltage". This tells me at a glance whether I need even bother
listening to it. I find a tape or CD player that won't give me
sufficient headphone output pretty infuriating.

I wonder how hard it would be to build a small headphone amp? That
could come in *really* handy at times. Especially if it was small and
portable.

Sean

From sfraves-owner  Tue Jan 18 11:37:30 1994
From: WILL-E <kia@eden.rutgers.edu>
Date: Tue, 18 Jan 94 14:36:57 EST
Subject: Re: Sony Headphones -Reply
Status: 

> I've founds stats for headphones and speakers to be almost completely
> meaningless. The only meaningful metric is one's ears. 

Unfortunately I left the stats at my parent's house.  Off hand I can tell you
the following:  the V6 was a consumer line headphone (that you could get at
most dept. stores) while the 7506 are professional line (that can only be
found at specialty/pro music stores.  I could only find them at Sam Ash).
Also, the bottom end has been cleaned up.  The bass sounds better.

> The only stat I even bother to look at anymore is "Headphone output
> voltage". This tells me at a glance whether I need even bother
> listening to it. I find a tape or CD player that won't give me
> sufficient headphone output pretty infuriating.
> I wonder how hard it would be to build a small headphone amp?

Build an amp?  Look no further, this is one of the other selling points of 
the 7506.  The output is a *lot* louder than the v6.  I was really impressed 
by this.  Check it out & see for yourself.  Ack, I sound like a commercial!?!

Here are the stats on the V6:

Type:    circum-aural, closed
Driver units: 40 mm dia., dynamic type
Impedance: 63 ohms at 1KHz
Sensitivity: 106dB/mW
Rated Power: 0.5W
Power handling capacity: 1W
Frequency Response: 5-30,000Hz
Weight: Approx 230g (w/o cord)

From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan 19 00:26:24 1994
From: Fred Heutte <phred@well.sf.ca.us>
Date: Wed, 19 Jan 1994 00:26:15 -0800
Subject: F&F!!!
Status: 

 
Was this the SHIT or what!!!
 
Megaprops to the Friends & Family Massive . . . to Resonate, whose
preparation and patience were readily apparent . . . to Ethan & Bryce
and all the others who planned and spread the word and hauled the gear
and cleaned up the mess (which made me feel a little guilty over leaving
without helping, but circumstances &c . . .!)
 
I got into the Cosmic Launch Mode right at 9 pm for my first ever public
decktrip.  Overall, it was a big kick.  The list is below for posterity
such as it may be.  My mix&match skills, quite shaky anyway, were
put to the test by my first encounter with the ubiquitous Galaxy mixer
and the confines of a small space.  (But I have to say, after seeing the
Water Temple FMM video last night with someone holding an umbrella to
keep the rain off Markie Mark while he was on the decks that I have *no*
reason to complain, not to mention C II with "so much rain on the records
that the needle made a *wake*", dealing with conditions as they are is
part of the Calling . . . but I digress . . .)  However, I appreciated
the comments in favor of the tracks put forth.  It's certainly not the
last time I'll be doing this!
 
In retrospect, I thought briefly that I might have erred too much in
the deephouse direction, and I could have tranced quite a bit more
(hey, I could have just mixed together the entire new DIY double disc
collection with excellent results!), but actually on third-thought
I was pretty pleased/honored to have the easy task of starting any
old way I wanted to and presenting the sounds that intrigue/move me
the most right now.
 
And that alone would have been a lifetime highlight for me, but things
hadn't even "got to the *cool* stuff yet," not by a longshot.  The rest of
the party reached cinematic levels, and I'm sure we all saw diferent
versions of*that* movie! In my case, I spent most of the time cocooned
in the chill space, and ventured into the garage at length only at the
end.  I was very highly impressed by Bryce's fine presentation and
especially by Amit's amazing relaxophonics, a smooth sailboat of live
trancey loops and keyboards that was perfect for my state of mind.
And Jesse's amazing dubtime, which had me almost convinced of trying
to talk him intohrowing in some of the Augustus Pablo stuff I have,
except I ended up not bringing it and I wouldn't generally want to impose
on another DJ's presntation in any event (but it was the thought that
mattered y'see!).  And Ethan, muttering at the end about playing house
for the first time ever in public ("Second!" corrected Bryce) but the
perfect energy pickup after the long languid night of musical starsailing.
 
And all the DJs I missed or don't know ther names, whose presence built
the fabric we all rolled around in, hanging/meditating/discussing . . .
The sheer level of musicality and excellence in this crew just amazes me.
As a little button I have says, "Creativity is intelligence having fun!"
This was one of the few parties I spent more time relaxed into the music
instead of dancing because I realized that any choice I made at the time
would be the correct one.  Yowsa & selah . . .!
 
The New School, the re-evolution of rave.  Amazin', ain't it!
 
I can't wait to hear all the tapes, although mine will sound a bit rough
(I managed to hit the line instead of cue switch once and dropped a few
seconds, plus the mis-hit mixes and, y'know, rookie errors but what the
hell!).  I was especially pleased to model the weh-kewl uk-dance shirt
and spin 'Disintegrate' in honor of Taylor 808 and the ne-raves crew, and
Mike, Randall and Jim and the Twitch collection which is the core of my
new obsession and one hell of a body of great musical work.
 
 
 
Friends & Family
Blue Cube
162 28th St, San Francisco
15 January 1994
(draft - may be errors in track order)
 
Wally Badarou: Chief Inspector
E.U.: Somebody's Ringing That Door Bell
Bohannon: Foot Stompin' Music
Thursday Club: Bless Da Funk
Kevin Saunderson: Power Base
King Akeen: Let the Rhythm Flow
Knowone: Never
The Formula: The Ritual
West Coast Spice: Injoye
The Creator: Let There Be House
Rock 2 House: Where You Where
Matter: Underground
Serious Rope: Happiness
Delta Lady: Anything You Want
SAS: Amber Groove
Lionrock: Carnival
Siouxie & The Banshees: Shadowtime
Orbital: Remind
Slave to External: Disintegrate
Deep Pearl: Red October
Evergreen: Tomorrow Never Knows
Sensoria: Unreal
Gipsy: I Trance You
Country-Western: Positive Energy
 
 
~e

>From graham@us.oracle.com  Tue Jan 18 22:34:27 1994
Date: Tue, 18 Jan 94 22:33:03 PST
From: Graham Potter <graham@us.oracle.com>
To: sfraves@techno.Stanford.EDU
Subject: Greetings, and surveys, and such
Reply-To: graham%dlsun87@us.oracle.com


Finally I emerge from the dark recesses of sfraveland, lingering where
I can see but not be seen, into full fledged postmanship. In case you
aren't sure who I am, I'm Graham, the guy who disappeared for a year
into the war-torn Urban African hinterland, only to return to the
beautiful Bay and bounce around on the fringes of the UVC posse and
the Ramona/Cyborganic realm. Crazy red dancing thing on my arm and
hair that seems to hang a little longer each day, that's me.

Anyway, I'm writing to thank those of you who took the time to fill
out the "Stark Raving Survey" that I handed out to some upstairs at
the Blue Cube on Saturday night. Your responses provide a valuable
angle to the whole research project by showing a little of the
character of smaller undergroundier events that surround the
mainstream rave scene. For those of you who didn't fill it out (mostly
becuase I was too busy bugging out to Jon D's religious wizardry to
hand out any more), you'll have to catch us at another event. The word
is that we won't be posting the survey on the net, for reasons that
have more to do (I hope) with statistical balances than
technologyphobia. The idea is to survey people at the events.

I will keep this list informed of the results, possibly making the
final report available on line when it comes out, and I will try to
answer any questions you have. Thanks again, take care, keep on
bursting with that legendary and irrestable energy, smile to the
stars, and I'll see you on the dance floor.

BTW, my usual e-mail address is:   graham@cyborganic.com

Graham


--- End of forwarded message from sfraves-owner@techno.Stanford.EDU

From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan 19 15:43:47 1994
From: laura@soda.berkeley.edu (Laura La Gassa)
Date: Wed, 19 Jan 1994 15:43:04 -0800
Subject: hi
Status: 

Hello San Francisco!

I've been here for over a week and I don't think I've posted
anything to sfraves.

Let's see . . . Brian, Cece (my cat) and I have an apartment up
in Twin Peaks now.  Once we get everything unpacked we'll see 
about a house-chilling party.  We can't have a house-warming
one (with dance music) because rave-force music would cause 
eviction, but a chill party would work great. Humm, maybe *THIS* 
will convince that ambient DJ "Vitamin B" to come out of retirement!

I'm working down in Menlo Park and so far like it (I've only
been there for 3 days).  And the commute isn't bad at all --
50 minutes and the traffic isn't all jammed up since I'm heading
southbound.  Of course, this means my weeknight party choices are
a bit limited because I have to get up weekday mornings, but every
so often I can make an exception and come in late.  I intend to go
to SpaceLab tomorrow since I'm taking Friday off to wait for the
moving van to come and deliver my furniture.

Now for rave-related stuff (after all, this is sfraves):

Friends and Family at the Blue Cube was brilliant.  Thanks to
everyone for everything they did.  You all might not believe this,
but I'm actually a very shy person and hate going to parties where
I have to talk to people I don't really know.  Well, the vibe and
people were so great last Saturday that I didn't have a problem at
all.  I talked to a lot of people who I don't know (and who's names
I don't quite remember, unfortunately) and had tons of fun.

Something pretty funny happened while I was spinning:  since Rocky
was up next to me working with the CD player, people would come up
to him and complement him on the music if I happened to be bent over
digging through my crate.  

I really liked what Amit was doing with his music, and think Dr. Teeth
is a great performance name.  I used to adore the Muppet Show.

Anyway, thanks for everything everyone.  It's wonderful to move nearly
3000 miles to a new city and immediately feel a part of things.
What happened at the Blue Cube was EXACTLY what I meant when I said
that list parties shouldn't fail.  The set up was perfect, people
drummed up excitement and brought their friends, and the whole thing
worked.  Now that we know how to do it, let's do it again!  

Love and community,

Laura

From sfraves-owner  Wed Jan 19 17:37:33 1994
From: brycer@netcom.com (Bryce Ryan)
Date: Wed, 19 Jan 1994 17:37:58 -0800 (PST)
Subject: Together
Status: 

Well, this didn't quite do it for me.

I visited Together last night, at its new home at 1015.  I listened to
an excellent acid jazz set, and a fine transition from acid jazz into
house (with a brief stop at reggae and dub).  Unfortunately, the sound
systems were as loud as all get out.  I talked with the person who
identified himself as "in charge of the sound", to no avail.  Unfortunately,
whether i have picky ears or what, the adjustments just weren't enough
for me, and i left with my ears ringing for the rest of the night.

Bob's right about the crowd not picking up downstairs until about 1AM.
The upstairs never took off while i was there (unfortunately, because
the upstairs system seems much better than the one downstairs).

The decorations/ambience was first class, however, and the people, overall
were quite friendly.  too bad i just couldn't stand to be there.
--

From bbehlen  Thu Jan 20 10:15:23 1994
