Lee, I wouldn't have expected *you* to beat me up in public...  I'd have
taken this private, but "hand-wringing and whining" are fightin' words,
pardner, so I've got to respond to your rose-tinted misconceptions. =)
And if you promise not to get personal I'll even let you have the last word...

> > The media set the agenda, so that the people themselves cannot. 
> 
> Right.  And I suppose that before the advent of mass media "the people"
> were setting the agendas for the power brokers of their time.

Well, you know there *was* France in the 1790's, Russia in the 1910's,
Germany briefly in the 1840's, Berkeley in '64, Paris in '68, Eastern
Europe in '89, etc. etc.

Every once in a while people DO become directly empowered...  The 1890's and 
1900's saw the rise of a powerful US progressive movement; the development of
Hearst-style yellow journalism and Spanish-American war jingoism was the
response that ultimately put the people back in their place...   But things
like the 40-hour work week or the end of the Vietnam war would never have
happened if not for the active involvement of huge numbers of ordinary 
but involved people.

> It is a simple fact that as distorted/slanted/innaccurate the info we get
> from the media is, people are more informed about what's going on in
> the world than they *ever* were.

Depends on how you define 'informed'.  We get oceans of carefully crafted 
"facts" from CNN, etc. but very little context with which to make sense of them.

> Call me an optimist, but ultimately,  I believe that truth will prevail
> - for those who want it....

OK, you're an optimist.  Now can I call you a taxi?  =)

(You see, my Marxism *is* of the Groucho variety! =)

It's the rare few who have the time, energy and perceptivity get a picture
of the world different from that of the propaganda machine -- consume and
don't ask questions.  Of course, we being on the Internet and especially
living in the Bay Area (not to mention being ravers) see things differently
but go to something like a sports bar in Pacifica sometime (like I did
during the baseball playoffs) and see what's really up with the American
psyche.  Or go up to Eureka and hang out with some loggers.  You'd be
amazed what a tiny minority we are.

> Today's lowest commom denominator is more accurate than yesterday's.
> Or would you prefer to have your tribal chief tell you that the gods
> demand a raid on a neighboring village.

This is a straw man argument -- never did I say things were necessarily
that much better in the past.  But at certain times before the turn of the
century in the US (and today in Europe) people were much more "in the loop"
with the political process than they are here and now.  And, I'm sorry, but
there's a world of difference between Maury Povich (or even Ted Koppel)
and Edward R. Murrow.

> > Mander 
> > (a former advertising executive) makes many cogent observations; one I 
> > happen to like has to do with the hypnotic, addictive trance-like state

No problem there, but be watch out for what memes get implanted in your head
when you're in those states, and who's implanting them!

> That's right.  And you - brought up watching TV - are somehow able to do
> this.  Amazing.

I grew up with people like Abbie Hoffman (and subsequently "Bob" Dobbs =)
teaching me how to pull the wool out of my own eyes!

I do believe that growing up with less TV would have made me a much more
focused person in many ways, and I'm sure I'd be much better read.

> I predict that interactive TV will eventually resemble the internet in
> many ways.  Why?  Because it is what many people want.

Some people want things like the Internet, but many more would be satisfied
with dozens of channels of interactive home shopping and Oprah and the latest
Schwartzenegger movie on demand.  Look in the business sections at what
kind of money companies like QVC, Paramount, Time-Warner, etc. are marshalling
to try to impose their view of the future on us.  The jury is out, but
we can influence the future with some effort and organization (no, I'm
not at all completely pessimistic...plus if anything I side with the
phone companies...)

FIRST Wax (A Preston production).  Man, he had a MULTI-COLORED laser, with
blue, green, white, and red, GOING OFF!!!  He also had the Archie Bell
dancers. Man, that party was the SHIT!

unvbelievable. Now, if there were a tape of *just* her....).  They had the
proper dress which made good use of BOTH the laser light, and the other
lights that were around (of course Erik Lutz was working the intellabeams
[a TRUE master at work]).  Along with that, and the laser making all kinds
of shapes/spaces with the smoke, and with the vibe of all 500 in
attendance, that party was THE one that night (March '92).  The music was
good too ;)

intense.  There have been other good light shows though, like the one at

the massives had to offer....oh yeah, another good show was the  first Let
Freedom Rave (I know that when those 3d lasers hit the side of that
mountain, and that E starting kickin in, I was done for!).  But nothing has
come close since.

Sometimes I miss the mega-non-LA-productions, if for nothing else but for
the visuals.

fucking cheap since *everyone* will have it.

From sfraves-owner  Tue Feb  1 14:02:25 1994
From: SCRUTON@JOYCE.dnet.hac.com
Date: 01 Feb 1994 14:01:56 -0800 (PST)
Subject: p'airfect rave
Status: 

Announcing the p'airfect rave (c) shite, inc :)

Greetings, Ravers young and old alike! For this once-in-a-lifetime event,
  you'll be presented with your airline tickets, whether you be in
    SF, LA, or Seattle.  All aircraft depart promptly at midnight, so
      be on time, and bring yer warm-weather gear (hint!)

Each of our sumptious Boeing 747's has had it's interior gutted of the
  dreary seats you are accustomed to seeing, and has been outfitted
    instead with beanbag chairs (w/ seatbelts, de rigeur!), swinging
      chairs hung from the ceiling (great during turbulence!) and, of
        course, lotsa lounge seating for those who want to conserve
          energy for the main party.  The dome lounge has been converted
            to an ambient/trance area, and the main lower floor is
              divided up into soundproof areas, with the fastest BPM
                being in the center area (most structurally sound :)

After 8 hours of flight/raving, the party should be warmed up (did I mention
  the nitrous/oxygen mix in the air system?)

As the planes begin to descend to their destination, the sun will be just
  coming up, and you will find your eyes blessed with the beautiful lagoons
    of Bora Bora, in French Polynesia, 4000 miles from traffic, air pollution,
      and crowds, with nothing between you and nature but yer skivvies. No
        problem landing on the outer reef, since it was built to handle
          large military aircraft.  After taking the boat from the outer
            reef to the main island (where we have graciously chartered 
              the local Club Med village for those sleepyheads who need
                their batteries charged), you will find your party-boats
                  ready.

The main event will take place on a 2 acre coral islet, known as Motu Tapu,
  once the playground for Tahitian Royalty hundreds of years ago.  This
    little island is surrounded by blindingly white sand and waters of
      every shade of azure your mind can picture.  The sound system has
        already been airlifted in, and is cleverly concealed amongst the
          palm trees, so no electronic equipment is visible whatsoever.
  For those of you who like to snorkel and sample the irridescent fishes
    and reef animals, we've hooked up a radio/sonar underwater transmission
      system, complete with special underwater headphones designed to
        receive these frequencies.

Towards sunset, the locals (Tahitians INVENTED the all-night party) will
  start to arrive, complete with all sorts of interesting things they
    have grown up in the jungles of the island, and the sunlight will
      cast a yellow glow on the 4,000 foot jagged mountain in the center
        of the island, a mountain so steep no one has ever climbed it.

The clouds will part as they go around the island, the rain will be drawn
  to the mountain, and the dolphins will begin to breach all around in
    the laggon (did I mention the free shark-rides, courtesy of the
      locals from Rangiroa?)

Yes, all this and more can be yours if you all get together and pool yer
  resources!  Towards midnite, as the incredibly intense southern stars
    come up, we'll light up the lagoon with some special halides we 
      brought in just for this occasion, and you will witness the wonder
        of a coral reef in full bloom, you will have fun feeding moray
          eels (quite friendly when stuffed with food), and don't forget
            the whale watch outside the reef (if the sea isn't too choppy)

After 4 days of tropical hedonism, the flights will depart back for the
  US (yup, we'll have to drag you kicking and screaming). Not to worry,
    we'll up the nitrous mix in the air coming back.

so, any takers :)

Dave Scruton
Fractallonomy

From sfraves-owner  Tue Feb  1 14:10:35 1994
From: Robert Jesse <rjesse@us.oracle.com>
Date: Tue, 1 Feb 94 14:09:26 -0800
Subject: Re: MDMA & neurons
Status: 

Tanya Smith wrote:

>In case you people don't know, low serotonin levels are responsible for
>depression, obsessive-compulsive behavior, suicide, eating disorders, etc.
>Violent behavior is also a result from screwing with these fragile
>receptors.  So look before you leap.  If you already have low serotonin
>levels, prolonged use of extasy could exacerbate your problem.

seems to me tanya is on track, though i would prefer to say "have been  
associated in some individuals with" rather than "are responsible for".   
researchers find a very wide range of serotonin metabolite levels in "normal"  
humans - low serotonin levels are not by themselves indicative of any  
disorder.

one study (Ricaurte & McCann) found that there was an average (with high  
variability) of 30% lower levels of a serotonin metabolite in the  
cerebrospinal fluid of a group of MDMA users (averaging some 75 MDMA sessions  
each) compared with a control group of non-MDMA-users.  the only functional  
differences noted between the two groups was that the MDMA users "reported  
less impulsive and hostile personality traits, and general constraint and  
control."

for a lucid description of the wonders of the serotonin system, see  
*Listening to Prozac* by Peter D. Kramer (Viking 1993).  the entire book is  
worthwhile, but note pages 134-136 especially.

for those who are concerned about the possibility of serotonin level or  
serotonin system changes in humans with therapeutic doses of MDMA, some  
researchers reckon changes can be lessened or prevented by taking  
antioxidants.  In an article titled "Phenethylamines, Free Radicals, and  
Antioxidants" (MAPS Newsletter, Volume IV Number 1), author Brian Leibovitz  
suggests in Table 1 taking as a preventive measure the following:  5 mg  
B-Carotene; 2 grams Bioflavonoids; 100 mg Coenzyme Q10; 2-4 grams L-Ascorbic  
acid; 1 gram L-Carnitine; 2 grams N-Acetylcysteine (NAC); 250 ug Selenium,  
and 1,000 IU Vitamin E.  "There is nothing magic about the doses listed; it  
is my best estimate based on present knowledge in nutrition."  i would add  
that if you don't feel like buying out the local vitamin store, taking a  
subset of these (even just the vitamin C) could well be helpful.

and, if you're really concerned, recent non-human animal research suggests  
that most or all of the serotonin system changes may be prevented by taking  
Prozac (fluoxetine) 0-6 hours after taking the MDMA (see McCann and Ricuarte  
in J. Clinical Psychopharmacology, 13 (3):pp. 214-217, 1993).  one might  
speculate that other SSRI drugs (Zoloft, Wellbutrin, Paxil) may work too.   
note, however, that some people report that Prozac taken before or in the  
first portion of an MDMA session lessens some of the desirable effects of the  
MDMA.

my synthesis of all this information is that there are a great many questions  
unanswered by research as yet - thus it's prudent to figure that the risk of  
some kind of subtle neurological "damage" in humans from MDMA use is not  
zero.  yet there is no emperical evidence of "damage" in humans (and there is  
considerable evidence of benefits) - this in many years of legal use (before  
1986 in the US), and quite widespread illegal use since then.

given a non-zero risk, it makes sense to examine the benefit side, and take  
the drug only when you expect to get some tangible positive outcome from it  
that you feel makes taking the risk worthwhile.

    massives:

    the perfect rave would feel like safe sanctuary where people
    can do the things people do at raves without worrying about
    being busted/hassled.  the perfect rave would have many options
    of music slow/fast loud/soft and some inbetween.  a live act
    near the middle.  the sound system must not be over the top
    causing distortion.  there should be no displeasure zones of
    sound.

    eye candy visuals are a must, hopefully something that builds
    and changes and isn't just loops.

    some kind of ceremony to tie it all together...some kind of
    empowering theme.

    local djs to warm things up, known miracle workers to do the
    climax then go free style after that.  live techno/new djs/old
    djs whatever fits the situation.  rave compatible entertainment
    happening simultaneously.

    a place where people could talk would be nice too.  maybe an
    area to dispense info/enlightenment on issues near and dear to
    the community.

    renegades/outdoors:

    the perfect rave would be fairly small, 200 tops.  sanctuary
    applies here too.  but the format is extremely low key.  the
    only other requirement here is a descent mobile sound system
    and great djs.  being outdoors provides the visuals if the
    site is right.

    the single most important ingredient for any rave is positive people
    who want to party

    barry
	

From sfraves-owner  Tue Feb  1 17:23:11 1994
From: anthrax@uclink.berkeley.edu (Ann Elizabeth Loraine)
Date: Tue, 1 Feb 1994 16:36:35 -0800
Subject: X and sleep
Status: 


Several people have told me that for a few nights after taking X they've
experienced more vivid dreams than usual and that they remember their
dreams in greater detail.  (These two phenomena are probably related, of
course...)  I've personally experienced much greater sensitivity (?) or
awareness to other people's emotions, body language, whatever for maybe
a week or so after the initial fun wore off.  One person I know says he's
experienced psychic episodes afterwards, while another friend told me it
cured her of a depression that had been crippling her mood for weeks.  

It's hard to separate out the effects of the drug from the effects of the
fun events experienced while under its influence, of course.  i'm usually
in a great mood for days after a rave, regardless of my substance intake!
But the effect on people's dreams seems to be a fairly dependable effect.

Does anyone else have any thoughts on this?

-Ann/thrax

From sfraves-owner  Tue Feb  1 19:06:34 1994

Status: 



From sfraves-owner  Tue Feb  1 19:06:52 1994
From: resonate@netcom.com (analog resonate)
Date: Tue, 1 Feb 1994 19:07:14 -0800
Subject: other numark uses: my view
Status: 

	preface:
	I am not a DJ. Nor do I have any desire to do normal DJ activities.
	What I am is a sound engineer. I work for very very high end
	professional digital audio gear company. I use very high end 
	sound equipment.

	story:
	I have many sources of sound in my room. I have cd players,
	a rack of electronic music gear, a radio, and a pink noise
	generator to use for sleeping. I have long searched for a simple
	elegant solution to mix and switch between all of these. The solution
	would have be useable in the dark and in non-sober states. It would
	have to sound good, be durable, work at consumer audio levels (-10db
	max), and be eventually rack mountable.
	I own a Mackie mixer but its life really lies in mixing instruments,
	not stereo line level sources although it does very well at that.
	I usually don't purchase normal consumer gear but I have been
	desperate for a solution to my mixing problem.

	result:
	Eventually I realized the answer to my problems was perfectly
	presented: a Numark DM1175 mixer. You can get them at Uncle
	Ralphs DJ supply on Telegraph near Amoeba.

	features: 4 stereo line ins with separate sliders. Mic in.
		  2 path xfader which fades between two of the 
		    line channels (which means you can use it for Quad!)
		  5 band stereo eq with a +15 db gain/cut. 
		  several other minor switching
		  cueing
		  meters
		  $300 out the door.

	praises: its very elegant, sounds great, and fits right on top
		 of my rack of electronic music gear. the EQ could
		 easily smash a sound system. the meters are big.
		 it operates at -10db nominal which is perfect if you
		 assume highs will reach 4db.

	criticisms: its noisy. really noisy. all switches make a "pop"
		    when activating/deactivating them. it has 60hz hum
	 	    everywhere but i haven't tried grounding the case
		    yet.

	I'll eventually use it for mixing music but until then its the
	perfect solution as a last-stage-before-the-amp mixer. Its
	fun to use. And if DJs ever stop by with turntables then hey-
	I got a mixer. and a DAT. and tons of original source material.

	(((((((((((resonate)))))))))))

From sfraves-owner  Tue Feb  1 22:19:26 1994
From: plunkett@uclink.berkeley.edu (Matthew James Plunkett)
Date: Tue, 1 Feb 1994 22:11:41 -0800
Subject: Recent MDMA research info
Status: 

I pulled this up from Biosis, a database at stanford similar to Medline,
for those of you who are interested.  If you want to search yourself, use
"
"f kw mdma and serotonin" or something like that.

I think that the take-home lesson from the study below is that it doesn't
take 20x the recreational dose of mdma to possibly mess you up.  But,
all these studies are done under unrealistic conditions.  (I.E. if you drank
2 12-packs of beer twice a day for four days, your liver would be damaged
and you might be dead.)  Many things are toxic at levels not too high
above what we normally take them at.  (Fugu, sodium pentothol, alcohol,
nicotine, etc.)

Anyway, here's the abstract!

TITLE:           Oral administration of 3,4-methylenedioxymethamphetamine
                   (MDMA) produces selective serotonergic depletion in the
                   nonhuman primate.
                 [Oral administration of 3 4 methylenedioxymethamphetamine mdma
                   produces selective serotonergic depletion in the nonhuman
                   primate]
AUTHOR:          Ali, S F (Neurochem. Lab., Div. Neurotoxicol., National Center
                   Toxicol. Res., Nctr Dr., Hft-132, Jefferson, Ar 72079-9052,
                   Usa.); Newport, G D; Scallet, A C; Binienda, Z; Ferguson, S
                   A; Bailey, J R; P
PUBLICATION:     Neurotoxicology And Teratology. 1993 15(2):91-96.
                 Neurotoxicol Teratol.
DOCUMENT TYPE:   Journal Article
LANGUAGE:        English
ABSTRACT:  MDMA (3,4-methylenedioxymethamphetamine) has been reported to
   produce serotonergic depletion in nonhuman primates at doses as low as 2.5
   mg/kg (1-2 times the typical human dose). The current study evaluated the
   dose-response relationships of MDMA (1.25-20.0 mg/kg) using regional
   concentrations of serotonin (5-HT) and its metabolite, 5-hydroxyindoleacetic
   acid (5-HIAA), and home cage behavior as endpoints. Adult female rhesus
   monkeys (n = 16) were treated orally with 0, 1.25, 2.5, or 20.0 mg/kg MDMA
   twice daily for 4 consecutive days. Eighteen behaviors were measured in the
   home cage prior to, during, and after MDMA treatment. One month after the
   last dose, the animals were sacrificed and brains dissected into several
   regions for neurochemical analyses. 5-HT and 5-HIAA were analyzed via
   HPLC/EC. The lower doses of MDMA (1.25 and 2.5 mg/kg) did not significantly
   alter 5-HT or 5-HIAA concentrations in any brain region except hippocampus
   in which 5-HT concentrations were decreased after 2.5 mg/kg. MDMA at 20.0
   mg/kg significantly decreased 5-HT and 5-HIAA concentrations in several
   cortical and midbrain structures. However, 5-HT and 5-HIAA concentrations in
   brain stem and hypothalamus were not significantly altered after any dose of
   MDMA. Combined with previous data from this laboratory, these results
   indicate that the decreased concentrations of 5-HT and 5-HIAA in selected
   brain regions show a selective dose-response relationship for MDMA-induced
   neurotoxicity as measured by  serotonergic depletion in the nonhuman
   primate.

-matt

was said by someone (a news anchor person I believe) in an
interview with Koppel.  He went on to say something about keeping
news interesting so people will stay tuned for the commercials.

It seems that they didn't succeed in keeping the news interesting,
now there's only 5 minutes between commercials. :)

If you didn't already know what the news is really for...

From sfraves-owner  Wed Feb  2 00:55:16 1994
From: Sameer <sameer@soda.berkeley.edu>
Date: Wed, 2 Feb 1994 00:26:24 -0800 (PST)
Subject: Anonymous mail service up for alpha testing
Status: 

-----BEGIN PGP SIGNED MESSAGE-----

	I've written a small anonymous mail service, and it's now
available for testing. There's no security, and I'll be keeping logs,
so don't think that it's secure, in any way. It's also running on a
PPP link which isn't connected all the time, so it's rather flaky.
	(I'll set it up as a real service once I get a real link-- if
anyone else wants to do it, they're welcome to use my code.)

	How to get an anonymous account:

	Send mail to admin@infinity.hip.berkeley.edu -- include in the
message a login, a "Full Name", a choice of remailer, and an encrypted
return address block encrypted with that remailer's public key.
	I'll set it up.

	How the anonymous account works:

	Someone will send mail to
login@infinity.hip.berkeley.edu. Then the system looks up in a table
which remailer is associated with that login. It then sends out mail
to that remailer, starting with the contents of the encrypted return
address block, then a "##" and then all of the message to
login@infinity, with "Received" lines taken out.

	Thus once the message gets to the last remailer of the chain
in the encrypted return block, the ## pasts the identifying
information of the person mailing to login@infinity.hip in the header
of the message. (It *should* do that...) If the person mailing to the
infinity address would like anonymity he/she should use an anon-mailer
on his/her end.

The encrypted-return address you send me should look like:

::
Encrypted: PGP

- -----BEGIN PGP MESSAGE-----
etc.

	Make sure you include that ::/Encrypted or the remailer which
gets it won't know that it's PGP encrypted.

	Remember, this is just setup for testing. Don't use it for
real applications.

- -Sameer

From sfraves-owner  Wed Feb  2 01:47:50 1994
From: crunch@netcom.com (John Draper)
Date: Wed, 2 Feb 1994 01:48:26 -0800
Subject: Perfect rave
Status: 

Perfect rave
============
Mike Romo Says...

>There has been some talk of the Perfect rave, and I was just thinking that
>instead of talking about it, we should just make it happen.

RIGHT ON!!

For me,  a perfect rave would be an outside rave,   preferrably a
meadow in the woods,  weather fairly cool.    With camping areas out
in the remote fringes far enough away from the music to make talking
easier.

The closest thing that came to a perfect rave was "Penalepes Web"
held way up in the hicks near Willits,  at a remota farm which had
beautiful gardens,   a mud pool,  plenty of water,  and a swimming
hole fairly close.   The next perfect rave was LoveStock held out
near Modesto at a fishing camp along the San Juaquin (Or was it the
Sacramento) river.  Multi-color lights along the banks of the river
was making some awsome visuals that lit up the fog setting on the
river at night.  Pieces of tree branches in the river had added an 
eery feeling to the scene.

I attended a number of outside raves,  with some having multiple dance
areas,  but to make the rave a perfect one,  I would want to have at
least one dance area play hardcore or hard acid trance.   Yow!!  Super
fast acid trace in the woods.... Now THATS! utopia...

CC
